Implementation Measures for the Prohibition of Opium in Various Counties and Cities of Anhui Province; Soil Paste Shops Must Register with the Civil Affairs Department; Smokers Must Obtain Licenses and Pay a License Fee of Two Yuan 79

Wuhu Correspondence: Since Anhui Province established a special tax for the prohibition of opium, there have been many merchants and opium soil and paste can be bought everywhere. Recently, the provincial government issued provisional measures for the implementation of opium prohibition in various counties and cities throughout the province, stipulating that anyone who wants to be a soil paste shop and smoker must follow the regulations and apply for registration with the Department of Civil Affairs in order to be quick. Smokers must apply for a smoking cessation license and pay two yuan. The measures are as follows: (1) The registration and registration of soil paste shops and smokers in various counties and cities shall be handled by the respective counties. In the cities of Anqing, Datong, Wuhu, Bengbu, Tunxi, Zhengyang, and Linhuai, it shall be handled by the respective Public Security Bureaus. However, rural areas not under the jurisdiction of the Public Security Bureaus shall still be handled by the county governments. (2) Opium cessation affairs in various counties and cities should be handled by the opium dens established by the county governments and Public Security Bureaus, or entrusted to local public and private hospitals. (3) When counties and bureaus apply to the Department of Civil Affairs for smoking cessation licenses and travel permits produced by the Special Tax Office of Hubei, each smoking cessation license should first be advanced with two yuan, and the travel permit should be advanced with one yuan and five jiao. (4) The number of soil paste shops in each county and city shall be quickly determined by the county governments and Public Security Bureaus, taking into account local conditions, and submitted to the Department of Civil Affairs for review and approval within ten days after receiving these measures. A letter shall be sent to the Special Tax Office for verification and reported to the provincial government for record. (5) Anyone who wants to be a soil paste shop must follow the provisions of Articles 8 and 10 of the Soil Paste Shop Regulations and prepare one-quarter of the first phase of the annual license fee according to the grade, together with a reliable business number term of one-quarter of the second phase of the annual license fee, and report it to the county government or Public Security Bureau for assessment and verification. The matter shall be forwarded to the Department of Civil Affairs for approval. Without the approval of the Department of Civil Affairs and the issuance of a license, it shall not be allowed to operate without authorization and shall not directly apply to the Special Tax Office for issuance in order to show uniformity. In addition to the foregoing procedures, anyone who wants to be a soil paste shop may directly apply to the Department of Civil Affairs in accordance with the regulations in order to be quick. (6) At the end of each month, each county and bureau shall separately list the number and number of licenses issued and received, as well as the revenue and expenditure deposits and withdrawals, and report them for investigation. The funds required by its opium cessation agencies must also be prepared in advance and approved before they can be used. (7) Before the establishment of the Opium Prohibition Office of the Department of Civil Affairs, the funds that should be paid according to regulations for the licenses issued by the Special Tax Office of Hubei must be paid separately to the Department of Civil Affairs to clear the procedures. (8) The license fees obtained by each county and bureau, in addition to the approved expenditures, if there is any surplus, shall be transferred to the successor after making a register when the old and new are handed over, and shall be reported to the Department of Civil Affairs for record. (9) Opium prohibition matters in various counties and cities may be handled by the Department of Civil Affairs, taking into account local conditions, and assigning a chief auditor to assist the county government and Public Security Bureau. The required salary and official expenses shall be paid by the respective county and bureau from the two yuan of the license fee distributed according to regulations. (10) If there are any matters not covered by these measures, the Department of Civil Affairs may submit them to the provincial government for revision at any time. (23rd)

Wuhu Electricity Strike; The Whole City Has Stopped Using Electricity for Two Days 80

Wuhu Correspondence: Stores and residents in Wuhu City, because the electricity price charged by Mingyuan Electric Light Company is particularly expensive compared to other ports. The price was increased again a year ago due to the increase in coal prices, but after the coal price returned to normal, the electricity price was not restored accordingly. Several requests for reduction have not been met. Recently, because the company revised its new regulations, the treatment of users is even more harsh. Therefore, the Wuhu Electric Light Users Association was organized to strongly request improvement and price reduction. Subsequently, the Commissioner's Office and the Public Security Bureau convened several meetings between the two parties to discuss mediation. The official decided on four measures and announced them for users to comply with: (1) The electricity fee will remain at 22 cents per kilowatt-hour; (2) The electricity base will be reduced by two kilowatt-hours according to the original table; (3) No labor costs will be charged for connecting electricity, and the materials will be paid for by the users, and the liquor money will be optional; (4) If the user believes that the installed meter has too many amperes, they can request the company to replace it with a smaller meter. However, the users believed that the electricity price still could not be reduced slightly, and it was particularly difficult to win in this time of economic depression. They still insisted on continuing to fight, and notified all users that they could pay the fee according to the price after the electricity price was resolved, and should not intentionally destroy it. The night before last, the Mingyuan Company sent personnel to the Kuishengzhai Department Store and Hat Shop at the intersection of Malu and Gongyuan Roads to collect electricity fees. The shop paid a certain amount first, and the remaining amount would be settled after the electricity price was resolved. The company insisted on not agreeing, and immediately cut off the electricity line, which immediately aroused the public anger of the prosperous district shops along Zhongshan Road and Siming Road. They unanimously turned off the electric lights and used candles and kerosene lamps to show their support. Suddenly, the city became dark and dim, and unusually desolate. The military and police authorities, because of the unstable situation at this time, the city-wide power outage, and the impact on local order, dispatched the entire team to maintain and persuade along the way. However, the users believed that this move was purely to promote the company's awareness. If the goal was not achieved, they would rather not use electric lights, and would never be coerced by the company. Until the evening of the 20th, the trend became more and more expanded, and the act of refusing to use electric lights had spread to the Fourth Pier and other places. The Shoe Industry Association and others also held emergency meetings one after another, deciding to ask all industries in the city to voluntarily stop using electricity to provide assistance. Recently, the Wuhu Workers' Organization Instructor's Office, because the trend was expanding and the relationship with local security was very important, issued a notice requesting representatives of both parties to meet at the office at 1 pm on the 21st to discuss a fair solution to avoid causing accidents. (21st)

Inspection Notes of Gan, Wan, Xiang, and E. Our Newspaper Special Correspondent Ren An. Overview of the Rural Economy of Zaoyang 81

Zaoyang Correspondence: Because the Zaoyang area is not very peaceful, there is still fear of wind and cranes in the poor countryside. Therefore, there is no news of other transfers of local garrison troops, and the local security team has increased without decreasing. According to Mr. Wu of the First District Office of the county, the burden of the local people is, "The whole county has ten districts, raising 9,000 yuan per month, 40 yuan for the military salaries of the garrison, and 5,000 yuan for the security team expenses. In the event of war, victory condolences, and casualties, there are so-called military reception fees and bandit suppression subsidies, with many names, all of which are paid by the people. A Zhou family, with more land, pays more than 1,000 yuan a year in donations and money and food, which is not included. It can be seen that the suffering of the local area is really no less than that of the tenants." After inquiring about why the garrison needs to raise money locally, Wu replied, "All troops with the words 'New Compilation' or 'Independent' in their titles mostly raise their salaries locally. The garrison in our county is an independent 34th brigade unit. The brigade headquarters is located in Suixian. The security issues of the counties along the Xiang (Yang) Hua (Yuan) Road are mostly maintained by the brigade. All military needs are met. Because the military discipline of the brigade has been investigated by the government and is still not bad, a certain amount of money is allocated each month, and the rest is apportioned by the Suizao counties. Our county pays 4,000 yuan a month, which is still relatively light." Passing by the county government gate, I saw more than a dozen carts of grain, cattle, and horses piled up. I passed by again the next day, and what I saw was still the same. However, I felt that there were new ones coming. I strangely asked a car owner in ragged clothes whether they were here to store grain. After a long sigh, the car owner slowly replied, "This is the military rice dispatched by each village. We are in a hurry and there is no way to save ourselves. How can we store grain for future use?" I then asked whether the military rice dispatched was deducted from the 9,000 yuan allocated per month, or was dispatched additionally. The car owner seemed to have other concerns, and turned his head and did not answer.

Land concentration in various villages has mostly become a manor system. The relationship between rent and tenancy, most of the benefits absolutely belong to the local area. If the tenants do not have sufficient capital, there is no hope of farming. For the tenancy procedures, the tenants must pay a deposit to the local area, called Dingtou, also called Yaoke. The amount is arbitrary, with no standard. Generally, if too much Dingtou is paid, the amount of grain money (i.e., rent money, local customs, rent is paid in money instead of grain, called grain money) to be paid each year in the future can be reduced as appropriate, or even eliminated. For example, if there are ten mu of land, each mu is worth 200 strings (each yuan is worth eight strings), a total of 2,000 strings. If the entire land is rented out, the Dingtou can be paid up to 1,500 strings, and then the grain money can be exempted. If the relationship is deeper, there are those who pay taxes for the landlord, otherwise they will generally not care. If the landlord is wealthy and the tenant is reliable, the Dingtou can be paid with no strings, and then 120 strings of grain money must be paid each year. If 300 or 500 strings of Dingtou are paid, then the grain money can be reduced to 90 or 70 strings. In recent years, due to soldiers, bandits, and droughts, land prices have gradually fallen. In the past, many places with abundant seats and thick shoes were frequently in decline. Disputes over stealing farmland were often heard. The so-called "stealing farmland" (actually, the local area only calls it stealing) means that several tenants receive more Dingtou for one piece of land. After being discovered, there is no way to recover it, and the defrauded tenants have to divide the planting according to the number. General rural loans, the interest rate is mostly between 30% and 50%. There is a so-called "Big One Plus", which must pay 10% interest per month, otherwise the principal and interest will generate new interest. For example, if you borrow 10 yuan, you should pay 1 yuan of interest next month. It should be deducted when borrowing, and you actually pay 9 yuan. When the full month is due, you must pay 1 yuan of interest for the next month, otherwise the principal will be made into 11 yuan, and you must pay 1.1 yuan of interest next month. People who borrow "Big One Plus" are not only poor farmers, poor workers, and small business vendors. They often borrow it when they are in urgent need. As for the cruel example of borrowing grain exclusively for farmers, the suffering is even greater than this. Because farmers are subjected to various exploitations, every year at the end of the old year, they just borrow "Big One Plus" to settle old debts (commonly known as borrowing to pay debts). After the new year, they immediately feel a lack of food. To keep the family smoke unbroken, they have no choice but to borrow grain. Ordinary spring borrowing grain, once the new grain is harvested in the autumn, must be repaid. The novel tricks for repayment are as many as three. One is "borrowing grain and repaying grain", that is, borrowing one stone and repaying one stone and four dou, or even two stones. The second is "repaying money and repaying grain", that is, borrowing one stone of grain, and also making a good grain price. When repaying, in addition to repaying one stone of original grain, you must also add the price of one stone of grain according to the estimated good price. Regardless of whether the new grain rises or falls, the lender can maintain its original profit of lending one and repaying two. The third is "borrowing grain and repaying money". The amount of principal and interest to be repaid should be calculated in advance, or interest can be generated on time. As a result, the interest on the loan is always higher than the first two. It is heard that the county government has issued notices to ban the above-mentioned usury methods of borrowing grain and borrowing money. After all, it is difficult to save the stubborn customs and the extreme oppression of the borrowers for a temporary livelihood. They are also willing to drink poison to quench their thirst. It is harmful to the rural economy. I don't know where I will end.

Rural finance has reached the point of exhaustion. Garrison troops, in the name of the Chamber of Commerce, have issued tens of thousands of yuan of copper coins, but due to the limitations of the area, it is difficult to circulate outside the territory. Currently, when urging the autumn grain, each grain is calculated to pay 11 yuan in regular tax and 15 yuan in additional tax, which is too much. Therefore, the opening of the levy is much earlier than the deadline. Compared with previous years, those who complete the payment on time show a decline. Second and third deadlines must be increased by fines and handling fees. Those who have not completed the payment on the surface are indeed as so-called "dare to play the law and deliberately delay," but in fact, the anxiety in the hearts of the defaulting households is increasing day by day. It is heard that a few days ago, an old man from the countryside, because the tax on the recently pawned fields was found to have not been paid for this old field deed, according to the law, either the field deed would be invalidated, or a considerable heavy payment would be fined. The old man was shocked and burned his paper. The manic illness has not ended. The reporter visited the tax payment office and learned that this year's tax payment regulations are roughly that the tax amount is based on the contract price. For "pawned deeds," every 100 yuan should pay regular and additional taxes at 7 yuan within the 9th and 10th months, 8 yuan in the 11th and 12th months, and 9 yuan next year. For "purchase deeds," those who pay in the 9th and 10th months pay 13.2 yuan per 100 yuan, which increases to 15.1 yuan in the 11th and 12th months, and to 17 yuan next year.

The unit names of farmland, Shi and Mu are mixed. There is a difference between "big Shi" and "small Shi" in Shi, and there is a difference between "new face" and "old face" in Mu. The difference between old and new, big and small is always one or two times. The area is different in different regions, and the area size is also different. For example, each Mu of paddy field is usually only half of each Mu of plain dry land. Compared with plain dry land and hillside dry land, it is only one-third or one-quarter of it. One Shi in the southern area has as many as four Mu. One Shi near the city is only half a Mu. Land disputes are mostly due to this reason. Measurement is needed and cannot be delayed. Cotton production is the largest. The annual output value is about 8 million yuan. The northeast two townships produce miscellaneous grains such as wheat, millet, sorghum, and corn. The southwest produces rice and grain, which is enough to eat in a normal year.

The streets in the city are still tidy. There is a joint middle and primary school with nearly 200 students. The Confucius Temple occupies a large area. The construction is based on Qufu. The palace is magnificent and spectacular, and it is the crown of the counties in northern Hubei. However, in recent years, the doors, windows, equipment, and instruments stationed by the army have all been destroyed, which the villagers regret very much.

Songjiang Water Police Intercept Bandit Ship 82

Recently, there have been frequent robbery cases in various villages in the Shihudang area. In each case, four or five families were robbed in a row. The county government attaches great importance to this matter. The day before yesterday, two water patrol boats were specially dispatched to cruise near the area. After the two patrol boats arrived at Shihudang, they were governed in the Shutang area, and firmly registered and guarded the essentials. Unexpectedly, at about 12 o'clock last night, two suspicious ships were found on the port surface. When the boat was ordered to be watched, it avoided the patrol boat and sped away. The patrolmen fired row guns to show their power. The boat then leaned on the opposite bank, and more than a dozen people who spoke the Chaohu accent jumped out of the boat, carried things ashore and escaped. The patrolmen, because of the dark night, were afraid of accidents, and did not dare to pursue them. After inspecting the boat, there were only a few pounds of salt. The abandoned ships have been guarded by the patrol boats.

A Robbery at the Taicang Wang Weishen Family Home 83

Wang Weishen's family, farmers in Beiyuan Township, West Wisteria Gate Port, in the first district, were of modest means. They had two daughters, and sons-in-law named Zhao Fushun and Fushun were brought into the family. The day before yesterday (the 24th), at around 8 p.m., as the whole family, young and old, were about to go to sleep, suddenly more than a dozen robbers arrived. They were dressed in plain clothes, spoke in mixed accents, and carried items such as handguns, wooden sticks, hemp ropes, and candles. They broke into the house, herded the men, women, and children into one room, and tied them up with ropes. Scheduled Implementation of Agricultural Warehouse Loans 85

County Magistrate Yan Shenyu, to alleviate the rural economy, specially convened with the Farmers Bank and the Industry and Commerce Association to establish the agricultural warehouse loan plan for the 21st year. The Farmers Bank and various pawnshops in the countryside will handle the county's agricultural warehouse loans. This was reported in previous newspapers. It is now known that the county government specially issued a notice yesterday. All countryside agents for agricultural warehouse loans, when receiving pledged rice, are required to set the loan interest rate at 1.6% per month. The price of the rice received as collateral should be 70% of the market price. The amount of rice pledged per household should be at least five dou and at most ten shi. Countryside pawnshops will uniformly begin accepting pledges on December 1st. It is also stipulated that all pawnshops in the county's districts and sections acting as agents for pledge loans, if they require funds and are insufficient, may seek funding from the bank, but each period is limited to 100,000 yuan, guaranteed by the county government, the Farmers Bank, and the pawnshop association. It is also heard that the Farmers Bank's own warehouses in Qianqiao in the fourth district and Lishe in the fifteenth district will also begin accepting rice pledges and issuing loans on December 1st. The warehouse in Dongting Town in the tenth district will begin on December 15th, also operating rice milling and storage services for customers.

Tragedy Occurs in Changzhou When a Bomb Falls to the Ground 86

The Second Battalion of the 523rd Regiment of the 262nd Brigade of the 88th Division of the Army stationed in Changzhou, which had been protecting the railway (the battalion was responsible for the defense from Longtan to Henglin), was ordered to transfer. Battalion Commander Cui Yanfu, upon receiving the order, instructed the troops to move to Changzhou to garrison. The Fourth Company, led by Company Commander Cao Ying, was attached to Train No. 17, the Zhenhu train, on the 25th, arriving in Changzhou at around 10 a.m. At around 1:30 p.m., soldiers were unloading military supplies on the platform when a soldier named Yu Genhu, wearing a hand grenade, did not secure the ammunition, causing it to misfire, fall to the ground, and explode, killing him instantly. Zhenjiang Court Tries Corruption Case 87

Cheng Zhuang, the former Chief of the Fifth District of the Water Police, followed the late Premier in the revolution for many years and has a deep understanding of the Party and the nation's history. Since taking office as the Chief of the Fifth Water District in the 20th year of the Republic, he has strived to reorganize the district, but due to salary arrears, he was unable to implement his plans. Although he knew it was difficult, he repeatedly submitted his resignation, but it was not approved until September of last year, when his resignation was finally approved on September 28th. He was ordered to hand over the district the following day. Due to the district's defense spanning hundreds of miles and the vastness of the area, he was unable to complete the handover in a hurry. Zhao Zeshao, who took over, suspected that Chen had been negligent and falsely reported to the provincial government that Chen and the accounting director, Gao Xiang, had not only embezzled public funds but were also suspected of misappropriation. The authorities, without investigating, arrested and detained Cheng Zhuang and Gao Tong. For thirteen months, they were neither interrogated nor investigated. After the reorganization of the provincial government and the arrival of Chairman Chen in the province, he learned about the case and ordered it to be transferred to the court according to law. Prosecutor Zhu of the Prosecutor's Office conducted several court investigations and found that the two were not suspected of committing a crime. According to civil law, Chen must first complete the handover. Therefore, the court approved the request of Chen and Gao to be released on bail of 30,000 yuan to complete the handover. The two were released on the 22nd. It is now known that the Prosecutor's Office has concluded its investigation and believes that Cheng and Gao are not suspected of committing a crime. Yesterday, it was decided to dismiss the case. As for Cheng's handover, Cheng and Gao are working to complete it, and there is no shortage of funds. People have been hired to create separate registers for reporting.

Pinghu Editor's Frame-Up Case Verdict 91

Yao Shuizhang, the editor of the Social Daily, is the son of Yao Baoxing, a clerk. He is idle and known as a jack-of-all-trades. Since printing the Social Daily, he has been causing trouble everywhere. A few days ago, he and Li Zhong, a former policeman, went to Fuzhen Temple outside the North Gate, posing as anti-smoking personnel, planting smoking paraphernalia, hoping to extort money. They were arrested by local people and monks and sent to the county. After a preliminary trial by Judge Tu Zhiping, they were ordered to be released on bail. The restaurant, terrified, immediately sent Yao Shuizhang to the county and requested to withdraw the bail. The judge approved it. Yesterday, Yao Shuizhang was sentenced for attempted fraud, fined 40 yuan, and the crime of impersonating a public official was leniently waived.

Yan Huizhong Kidnapped in Shizong, Huzhou 92

In the Xihuijiao area, about two li from Shizong in the southern countryside of this city, there is a resident named Yan Huizhong, 40 years old. His assets are not abundant, and he relies on two harvests a year to make a living. On the afternoon of the 23rd of this month, at about 6 p.m., a bandit ship suddenly arrived, with more than a dozen bandits armed with guns and other weapons. They swarmed ashore and went to Yan's house and knocked on the door. Yan was having dinner and heard a commotion outside, suspecting something was wrong, so he opened the door himself. The bandits, seeing Yan, immediately pointed a gun at him, forbidding him to make any noise. They then kidnapped Yan Huizhong and took him onto the ship. Two bandits guarded the hostage on the ship, while the other bandits searched the house, taking more than a dozen pieces of clothing and three silk quilts. After the robbery, the bandits returned to their ship and headed towards Shizong.

Dujiaying, Mingguang Robbed Twice 93

Dujiaying in the west countryside was robbed by bandits last month, and the son of resident Du Peilan was kidnapped and has not yet been redeemed. Unexpectedly, the night before last (the 24th) at about 12 o'clock, dozens of bandits came again and searched the entire village, looting all the livestock and urging Du to redeem the ransom ticket. Before leaving, they burned a haystack.

Three Notorious Bandits Executed by Firing Squad 94

The Provincial Security Special Service Battalion captured notorious bandits Zhang Fei, Ma Hongcai, and Wang Xiaodaozi in the west countryside of Dingyuan, and handed them over to the county government for legal action. After interrogation, they confessed without denial and were sentenced to death. Yesterday, County Magistrate Sun executed the three bandits by firing squad.

Letter　Letter from the Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau 95

To the editor: I recently read in the Zhenjiang newspapers of the 25th of this month that the land survey fees for the twenty counties north of the Yangtze River would be temporarily suspended. This is not consistent with the facts. According to the original resolution of the 613th meeting of the Provincial Government Committee on the 24th of this month, the land survey fees for the twenty counties north of the Yangtze River that have not yet been levied will be temporarily suspended. The Finance and Civil Affairs Departments and the Provincial Land Bureau will discuss the annual amount of land survey fees to be levied and report to the meeting for further discussion. This case only applies to the eleven counties of Yiwei, Gaoyou, Fengcheng, Funing, Xinghua, Siyang, Tongshan, Fengxian, Xiaoxian, Dangshan, and Muyang north of the Yangtze River that have not yet reported the start of the levy. These counties have special circumstances, and it is proposed to adjust the levy amount to alleviate the difficulties of the people. Once the departments and bureaus have discussed and decided, and the meeting has resolved, it must still be implemented. The remaining nine counties of Taixing, Huaiyin, Lianshui, Suqian, Peixian, Pixian, Suining, Donghai, and Ganyu have all reported the start of the levy at various times and have already collected a certain amount, and are not included in this category. I am afraid that the reprint is inaccurate, leading to misunderstandings. I am writing to ask your newspaper to check and include it in the letter column to make corrections. Sincerely, Jiangsu Provincial Land Bureau, November 25th.

Zhang Yuejun Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss the Current Situation of Hubei Province's General Administration Revenue and Expenditure of Recurring Expenses Match Temporary Expenses Are Very Difficult Construction of Highways, Telephones, etc. Has Basically Been Completed Bandits Will Be Eliminated Actively Preparing for Relief Issues 98

Central News Agency reports: Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, has been in office for nearly five months, and the province's political affairs have made considerable progress. Therefore, he went from Hubei to Jiangxi and then to Nanjing a few days ago to report the current situation of the province to the central government. Zhang also left Shanghai for a long time, so he arrived in Shanghai from Nanjing at 8 a.m. yesterday to meet with old friends in Shanghai, and decided to return to office with his family in two or three days. A Central News Agency reporter visited Zhang at his residence yesterday morning to inquire about the current situation of bandit suppression, construction, and finance in Hubei Province. He gave a very detailed explanation, which is recorded as follows:

Hubei Province's Finances Are Still Difficult 99

Zhang said that Hubei Province's finances are still difficult because of insufficient revenue and large expenditures. In the past, the province's revenue was more than 20 million yuan, but since the province's salt tax surcharges and other revenues were sent to the central government, and because of disasters, the people have been unable to make a living. Therefore, since the 20th year of the Republic, revenue has decreased significantly, with only 6 million yuan per year. On the expenditure side, the annual cost is more than 13 million yuan. After offsetting revenue and expenditure, there is a shortfall of more than 7 million yuan. Fortunately, the central government subsidizes 200,000 yuan per month, and the General Headquarters subsidizes 400,000 yuan per month, a total of about 7.2 million yuan per year. Therefore, since the second half of last year, revenue and expenditure have been able to match. The current financial situation of the province, under the heading of recurring expenses, has no difficulties. However, temporary expenses are still difficult and need to be addressed. As for construction costs, there are only tens of thousands of yuan this year, but construction projects in the province are waiting to be carried out and funds are urgently needed. At present, this item of expenses is allocated from the national economic committee highway fee item. Zhang also said that Hubei Province's land tax revenue is still very different from that of other provinces, so Hubei people's burden is lighter than that of any other province. I will reorganize Hubei's finances by starting with cleaning up the malpractices of corruption, in order to increase revenue, and will not proceed from the perspective of opening up new sources of income, because Hubei people have suffered disasters for a long time and cannot bear any further burdens.

Measures Have Been Taken to Relieve the Rural Areas 100

Regarding the progress of construction in the province, in terms of highways, a total of more than 2,000 kilometers have been completed or are about to be completed. The installation of telephones in various counties has also been completed in order. As for rural relief, (1) a farmers' bank has been established in the province to provide loans to farmers when the new crop is not yet available, and expansion has begun to popularize it throughout the province; (2) planting is being improved to increase income, such as cotton planting, which has now begun to be improved, and a special agency has been set up to manage it; (3) the food relief plan is now being implemented in accordance with the plan resolved at the Nanchang Eight Provinces and Cities Food Conference. The above three items have been handled properly, and other construction projects in the province will also be carried out separately as financial resources permit.

The Only Important Thing for Post-Bandit Areas 101

After the bandit suppression in Hubei Province, the large bandit gangs have been eliminated, but there are still scattered remnants, which are still being pursued. Therefore, the bandit disaster in the province will soon be completely resolved. More than 20 counties have been recovered in the bandit areas. In these more than 20 counties, due to years of harassment by the bandits, the people's lives have been devastated to the extreme and are in urgent need of relief. Therefore, the post-bandit area relief issue is the only important thing in the province. The post-disaster relief funds are very large, and planning is now underway separately, including (1) subsidies from the central government, (2) requesting subsidies from all sectors of society, and (3) planning through a small amount of funding, so that a small amount of funding can be accumulated to save the people in the bandit areas. Hubei Province has already established a planning agency to specialize in this matter. I am grateful for the donations from all walks of life in Shanghai. Therefore, in addition to meeting old friends, I am also representing the people of Hubei Province to thank all walks of life.

Hope that Shanghai People Will Go to Hubei to Visit 102

Zhang continued, saying that the disturbance of the Red Bandits is a major disaster for the whole country. Therefore, bandit suppression work is not only the responsibility of the government, but also the responsibility of the people of the whole country. The people of the country should recognize this point, and the elimination of the Red Bandits can be expected. To make the people of the whole country understand, propaganda should be expanded, and it is hoped that the media will first promote it. The people of Hubei Province hope that representatives of various groups in Shanghai will organize a tour group to visit the bandit areas of Hubei Province to inspect the devastation of the bandit areas that have been recovered. It is especially hoped that the media will participate. If you can come, I will represent the people of Hubei Province and entertain you sincerely.

Four Provinces Sign to Reform the Provincial System 103

The reporter then asked about the change of the provincial system and what progress has been made now. Zhang replied that Chiang Kai-shek previously stated that the reform of county administration is of great significance to the progress of local politics, and at this time when everything is waiting to be done, the lack of county administration funds is especially felt. Therefore, he once had the intention of saving provincial government funds to sell to help county administration. The Third Plenary Session also discussed the bill to change the provincial system. After I arrived in Hubei, I suggested to Chiang Kai-shek that the offices of the various departments of the provincial government should be consolidated to save expenses. In this way, a lot of formalities for internal and external official documents can be saved. Chiang Kai-shek immediately sent my proposal to the provinces for their opinions. It is now known that the four provinces of Zhejiang, Jiangsu, Hunan, and Gansu have signed the reply. Although the opinions vary, they all agree that the existing provincial government really needs to be researched and revised. Chiang Kai-shek has decided to wait for the replies from the provinces to arrive before approving the method and ordering them to comply. As for the county fees in Hubei Province, it has been decided that from next year, each county will increase its expenses by 300 yuan per month to facilitate construction.

Extremely Saddened by the Fujian Incident 104

Regarding the central government's steps towards Fujian after the Fujian Incident, Zhang Qun, Chairman of the Hubei Provincial Government, told a Central News Agency reporter that he was extremely saddened by the rebellion of Chen Mingshu and others in Fujian. When he passed through Jiangxi, he met Chiang Kai-shek, and he did not know the details of the military situation in Fujian. However, solving the Fujian problem cannot be achieved by empty political methods and mediation. There should be military measures. Guangdong's attitude has been very clear, and all provinces are calling for a unified denunciation. The Fujian Incident will eventually be unsustainable.

East China National Salvation Army Zhang Zhichao's Troops Call for Help Send Scouts to Shanghai at Risk Request for Assistance with Clothing and Medicine 109

Far East News Agency reported that Zhang Zhichao, the commander-in-chief of the East China National Salvation Army, sent scout Yu Desheng, disguised from Dongxing Town on the black border, to Shanghai to report to Zhang Zhendong, the representative stationed in Shanghai, about the recent emergency war situation at the front and to ask Representative Zhang to urgently appeal to all sectors in the rear. A reporter from the Far East News Agency visited yesterday and was told in detail about the righteous army's resistance to the enemy. The following is a summary:

Coming to Shanghai at Great Risk 110

Our department's scout, Yu Desheng, came to Shanghai this time under the direct orders of Commander-in-Chief Zhang and Commanders Wang, to report on the latest war situation at the front lines and the vicious plans of the Japanese and puppet troops. Yu departed from Dongxing Town, near the border of Heilongjiang Province, disguised as a peddler with a willow basket over his shoulder. He walked to Harbin, where he was questioned by Japanese and puppet troops several times and detained overnight. Fortunately, he was not carrying any written reports; otherwise, his life would have been in danger long ago. Security has become ten times tighter than before. Because our troops at the front are fighting hard without support, he had to come here at great risk. Yu arrived safely in Shanghai yesterday morning (that is, the day before yesterday).

Melee in Xiji 111

Upon investigation, after our Commanders Wang Zhenqi and Wang Zhenfang recovered Chexing Town, they advanced victoriously to Xiji Factory. Unexpectedly, on the night of the eighth, Japanese and puppet troops arrived stealthily and launched a massive encirclement. Fortunately, our troops discovered them early and immediately issued an emergency assembly order. At that time, the enemy had already formed two layers of encirclement. Commander Wang, seeing the urgency of the situation and the danger of the entire army being wiped out, personally led the broadsword team to break through the encirclement in a melee. The enemy used machine guns to sweep and artillery to bombard. The battle lasted until dawn on the ninth, when the inner encirclement was broken. However, the outer encirclement was still very serious. They had no choice but to use melee combat to charge and fight their way out. Seeing that we were not afraid of death, the Japanese and puppet troops retreated and defended their original positions. Xiji Factory was thus recovered by us. Around 1:00 PM, after a headcount, we found that 490 of our troops were dead, including one battalion commander, one company commander, and two platoon leaders. 113 were wounded. Over 100 Japanese and puppet troops were killed by our broadswords, and 42 had their hands and feet cut off but were not dead. We captured six machine guns, two mortars, and a large number of guns and ammunition. This battle was particularly fierce, unprecedented this year. The Japanese army's fighting against our righteous army relies on their superior military supplies and adequate supplies. But when it comes to combat capability, they are far inferior to the righteous army.

Japanese Cruelty 112

The commander of the Japanese Kwantung Army stationed in Harbin held repeated meetings, ordering his troops to completely eliminate all righteous armies in the puppet territory from November 1st to December 16th. Notices were posted in public places, stating that anyone who concealed the residence of righteous armies without reporting it would be considered as having committed the same crime as the righteous armies. In areas where the righteous armies were defeated and retreated last month, countless families were slaughtered or subjected to brutal torture. This has only inspired the people to rise up and become righteous soldiers, fighting to the death against them.

Waiting for the Freeze to Launch a Joint Attack 113

Recently, the weather in Jilin and Heilongjiang has been severely cold. The Songhua River and its surrounding area are covered in thin ice, but it is not yet strong enough to bear the weight of people. The plan to wait for the ice to thicken slightly, then coordinate with Sun Chaoyang and other units to launch surprise attacks across the ice and advance on various locations, is now complete. Due to military secrets, it will remain confidential for the time being.

Urgent Need for Assistance 114

Our Commander-in-Chief Zhang Zhichao ordered Yu Desheng to come to Shanghai. Because the search along the way was strict, he did not use written reports but gave oral reports. He instructed me to personally go to Generals Zhu Ziqiao and Li Du's residences to report on the difficult situation at the front and request them to appeal to all sectors for urgent assistance, including cotton clothing, medicine, and other expenses. Because the current battle can be sustained temporarily, but when the severe cold comes and they have to launch ice attacks, they must have cotton clothing. Academic Organizations Prepare to Welcome Marconi, the Inventor of Radio 125

The world-renowned inventor of wireless radio, Italian Marchese G. Marconi, came to visit the Far East. He recently arrived in Japan and was warmly welcomed by the government and the public. Marconi is now traveling from Japan to Liaoning and is expected to arrive in Dalian within days and then come to Shanghai. The Academia Sinica, the United Office of Shanghai Universities, the Science Society of China, the Chinese Institute of Engineers, Jiaotong University, and the Chinese Wireless Radio Engineering School have jointly launched a welcome for Marconi. On the afternoon of the day before yesterday (the 25th), at 3:00 PM, a welcome preparatory meeting was held at the Science Society of China on Avenue Albert. Attendees included Zhou Zijing (Academia Sinica), Li Zhaohuan (President of Jiaotong University, representing the United Office of Shanghai Universities), Yang Xiaoshu (Science Society of China), Xu Peihuang (Chinese Institute of Engineers), but Xu was unable to attend due to business and delegated Shi Konghuai as his representative, Zhang Tingjin (Jiaotong University), and Fang Ziwei (Chinese Wireless Radio Engineering School). After discussion, it was decided to temporarily use the Science Society of China as the temporary office of the preparatory committee, organize a committee, and agree to hold a public banquet for Marconi at Ronghong Hall of Jiaotong University. Li Zhaohuan was publicly elected as chairman and was also asked to give a scientific lecture in the auditorium. A letter was first sent to Marconi through the Italian Minister, expressing welcome. At the same time, Xu Peihuang was recommended to contact the municipal government to discuss welcome matters. Fang Ziwei inquired about Marconi's whereabouts at any time and contacted local wireless radio communication circles such as the International Radio Station and the Broadcasting Station to discuss the date of reception. It was also decided to hold a second meeting next Thursday (the 30th of this month) to discuss all aspects of the welcome. From today, any circles willing to join the welcome can contact Mr. Yang Lishu, the secretary of the association. According to the latest news, Marconi and his wife will pass through Tianjin on the 29th of this month and go to Beijing on the 30th for a short tour. After that, they will go south from Tianjin and Beijing and are expected to arrive in Shanghai around the 7th or 8th of next month.

The River Conservancy Committee Discusses Loan from Boxer Indemnity, Second Phase of River Conservancy Project Being Prepared 127

The Ta Kung Pao reports that the initial project of dredging the Zhangfu Canal by the River Conservancy Committee was completed at the end of July. Navigation and irrigation have benefited greatly. The committee is now actively preparing for the second phase of the project and has discussed borrowing 9 million yuan from the Boxer Indemnity Fund for the project. The news is recorded as follows:

Borrowing from the Boxer Indemnity Fund for the Second Phase of the River Conservancy Project. It was previously decided that the project cost would be 9 million yuan, to be allocated from the Boxer Indemnity Fund. The toll revenue collected by each lock would be used as collateral, and the interest would be paid monthly by the Ministry of Finance. However, since Minister Song resigned, the procedures could not be fulfilled. Vice Chairman Chen Guofu of the River Conservancy Committee has repeatedly negotiated with Minister of Finance Kong Xiangxi and Chairman Zhu Jiahua of the Boxer Indemnity Fund. The result was quite satisfactory. The loan and repayment methods for the Boxer Indemnity Fund and various procedures have been largely agreed upon. However, the Boxer Indemnity Fund still insisted on disbursing the funds in three installments. The first installment of 4 million yuan would be disbursed on December 1st, the second installment of 3 million yuan would be disbursed on February 1st of the 23rd year, and the entire amount would be disbursed by the end of June. Chen believes that disbursing the funds in installments is feasible. However, the second phase of the River Conservancy Project is of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. If the project starts and the funds are insufficient, the work will be suspended, resulting in huge losses. Therefore, Chen is now negotiating with the Boxer Indemnity Fund to request a one-time disbursement, but the Boxer Indemnity Fund has not yet agreed.

Second Phase of the Project. As for the second phase of the River Conservancy Project plan, it was decided to first build the Huaiyin and Shaobo locks to maintain convenient navigation and traffic. Although ships can travel between Qingjiangpu and Zhenjiang, except for the area south of Gaoyou, which can barely be passable all year round, the riverbed in the Mapengwan section north of Gaoyou is silted up. Every winter, the river freezes and dries up, making navigation inconvenient and traffic interrupted. The River Conservancy Committee dispatched engineer Wang Fengxi, along with personnel from the engineering and land departments, a few days ago to survey the lock construction site and drill soil samples and handle land acquisition procedures. All work is now being prepared, and work can begin on a scheduled date as soon as the Boxer Indemnity Funds are disbursed.

Ministry of Industry Investigates Field Tax, Rice and Wheat Taxes, to Collect Reports and Research Improvement Measures, Seeking Convenient Transportation and Sales to Relieve the Rural Economy 131

The Ministry of Industry, because local levies and miscellaneous taxes are heavy, causing domestic rice and wheat to be unsalable, allowing foreign wheat and foreign rice to be imported, and the rural economy to suffer a major blow, in order to relieve rural bankruptcy, has specially formulated investigation forms for field tax and rice and wheat taxes, ordering county governments and county chambers of commerce across the country to investigate and fill them out, intending to study improvement measures. The city has received the order, which is recorded as follows: "Rice and wheat are essential food items for the people. The abundance of their harvest and the stagnation of their transportation and sales are of great importance to the national economy and the people's livelihood. It is the responsibility of the ministry to promote production to ensure sufficient food and facilitate transportation and sales to enrich the people. Now, in order to implement these measures, we have specially printed investigation forms for the production and sales of rice and wheat in each province and the field tax levied and the taxes collected, and distributed them to each county for widespread investigation, in order to understand the current state of production and sales and the advantages and disadvantages, so as to seek improvement methods. We are sending three copies of the field tax and rice and wheat tax investigation form for each county, and you must follow the items to investigate and fill them out in detail. You must mail one completed copy by registered mail to the ministry within seven days of receiving this document. Do not delay. Sincerely."

Silk Industry Decline: Producing and Selling Nations Urgently Seek Solutions, Actively Promoting Grand International Publicity, International Silk Conference on the Agenda, 丨Major Competition Between Natural and Artificial Silk Expected丨 132

According to the Industrial Society, silk fabrics have traditionally used natural silk as raw material. However, in the past five years, 60% of raw materials for silk fabrics have been replaced by artificial silk, greatly reducing the price and use of natural silk. Silk-producing countries have been hit hard, and China's silk industry, clinging to old methods and failing to innovate, has suffered even more due to the encroachment of artificial silk. The rise of artificial silk is not only due to its low price and consistent quality but also to its extensive publicity. In the past year, the Japan Central Sericulture Association proposed that natural silk producing and selling countries unite to promote natural silk to compete with artificial silk. However, due to financial difficulties, it was not implemented. This year, Italy specially sent Dr. Golliher, a member of the Italian Parliament and President of the Silk Association, to the United States to discuss silk promotion matters. Japan also sent Dr. Imai, the president of Katakura Silk Factory, and eight others to the United States for investigation and to carry out silk promotion work. At that time, Mr. Miao Zhongxiu, director of the Silk Department of the Chinese Commodity Inspection Bureau, also represented the Shanghai Silk Factory Association and the Jiangsu, Zhejiang, and Anhui Silk Cocoon General Office to the United States for investigation. Mr. Miao arrived in New York, and Dr. Golliher also arrived in the United States at the same time. They then met with Mr. Ganli, the former president of the American Silk Association, and others to discuss solutions. Mr. Ganli and others then united American silk industry leaders to initiate the organization of the International Silk Association, inviting various countries to participate. Japan, Italy, France, Switzerland, and other countries expressed their approval and agreed to send representatives to join. Mr. Miao recommended Ke Guoxian, Director of the International Trade Bureau, as an honorary member of the association on behalf of China. The association formally sent a telegram of appointment. Now, Mr. Ke has received a letter from Mr. Ganli stating that the association has been officially registered in New York State, and the Japan Silk Association has also decided to first subsidize the association with 50,000 yuan, so that the grand international silk promotion work can be launched. At the same time, a remittance was received from Dr. Golliher, stating that the International Silk Conference was held in Paris on November 13th, and issues such as silk price setting, silk production standards, and silk promotion were all included in the agenda for discussion. Based on this, the major war between natural silk and artificial silk has entered a stage of close engagement, and the future of silk sales is not optimistic.

Flour Mill Association Cables Requesting Exemption from Wheat Import Tax: Reason Given is that Domestic Production is Insufficient to Meet Consumption Needs, Requiring Foreign Wheat 133

In order to protect the interests of farmers, the central government has already decided through the Legislative Yuan to levy an import tax of 1.25 gold units per 100 catties of foreign wheat and 2.5 gold units per 100 catties of foreign wheat flour, which will be announced and implemented on New Year's Day next year. However, the flour industry in this city believes that even in bumper harvest years, domestic wheat is only sufficient to meet five months of consumption. After the import tax is levied, foreign wheat can certainly be prevented from being sold inland, but factories will have no raw materials to produce flour, and the wheat-eating provinces will also face the risk of food shortages, which must be carefully considered. The Flour Mill Association yesterday convened a meeting of thirteen manufacturers in Shanghai to discuss remedial measures. After consultation, they unanimously advocated requesting the central government to exempt wheat from import tax. The following is a transcription of the association's telegram to the Executive Yuan, Legislative Yuan, Ministry of Finance, etc.: "To Premier Wang of the Executive Yuan, Speaker Sun of the Legislative Yuan, and Minister Kong of the Ministry of Finance, Nanjing: Domestic wheat is usually harvested in May, and farmers have already finished selling their crops. The government now intends to aid rural areas, but imposing taxes at this time will not benefit farmers. If taxes must be imposed, it should be postponed until the beginning of the harvest in May next year for farmers to truly benefit. In bumper harvest years, domestic wheat can only supply flour mills for half a year. Wheat imports are a necessity. Even if a tax is imposed, it should only be a general commodity tax, 5% or at most 10% of the value, because this is a raw material to supply flour mills, not a product like foreign rice or flour being dumped. We hereby telegraphically submit this request for your consideration and approval. Respectfully, Gu Xinyi, Chairman of the Shanghai Flour Mill Association."

Taikoo Labor Strike: Officially Resolved in Guangzhou the Day Before Yesterday, All Workers of the Wusong Ship and Others Resume Work 134

According to the New Voice News Agency, the case of the British Taikoo Company expelling the midship workers of the Wusong ship has been delayed until now for eleven months. The day before yesterday, labor and management signed a settlement record at the Five Provinces Foreign Affairs Office in Guangzhou, and the labor dispute has been resolved. The following are the details obtained by the New Voice News Agency reporter:

Course of the Dispute 135

Since January of this year, when the Taikoo Company forcibly expelled all 128 midship workers of the Wusong ship, the Guangzhou Seamen's Union blockaded the port of Guangzhou from June 23rd and refused to unload Taikoo's goods. It was not until October 18th that the Taikoo warehouse inventory was extracted. In August, all stevedores, midship workers, stokers, watermen, stewards, and pilots, more than 100 employees of the Foshan ship between Guangzhou and Hong Kong, also announced a strike. The Foshan ship is still moored in Kowloon Bay.

Divergent Opinions 136

After the Guangzhou seamen went on strike, the Taikoo Company repeatedly changed representatives to mediate. As a result, the workers demanded 400,000 yuan in compensation for losses, but the company failed to sympathize, making it difficult to resolve. At the same time, due to the workers' blockade of the port, the Taikoo Company abandoned the Guangzhou route in July. All seventeen ships, including the Shanghai-Guangdong routes, Xinjiang, Shandong Jinan, Yingzhou, etc., have changed their routes.

Mutual Concessions 137

The Taikoo Company repeatedly asked Gan Jiehou of the Five Provinces Foreign Affairs Office in Guangdong and the manager of Jardine Matheson to mediate. Because the Hong Kong-Guangdong route is the main force of Taikoo's Nanhua class, Taikoo immediately built a new ship named New Foshan after all the workers of the Foshan ship went on strike. Its route is still between Guangzhou and Hong Kong. Taikoo first made concessions and accepted the workers' demands, but requested modifications to the overly harsh six measures proposed by the workers. The seamen also accepted the mediator's advice and gradually retreated.

Contract Signed and Resolved 138

At 2:00 PM on the 25th, a settlement record was signed at the Guangdong Five Provinces Foreign Affairs Commissioner's Office, mediated by the manager of Jardine Matheson's Guangzhou branch. The content was that the Seamen's Union's condition that Taikoo must hire workers through the Guangdong Union in the future was completely abolished. Only 128 midship workers of the Wusong ship and more than 100 of the Foshan ship were allowed to resume work, and it was guaranteed that similar incidents would not occur in the future. As for the compensation issue, the Midship Union announced it was 197,000 yuan, 25 yuan per worker. Another seamen's group said it was a total of 160,000 yuan, while rumors said it was 179,000 yuan. As to which number is accurate, the Midship Union has telegraphed Guangdong to inquire.

Jiangsu Provincial Government: Planning for the Jiangnan Seawall Project, Requiring 1.2 Million Yuan, Requesting Central Government to Allocate Funds for Repair 143

According to the Dagon News Agency, the Jiangsu Provincial Government believes that the Baotai-Changsong-Jiangnan Seawall, stretching for hundreds of miles, is the barrier of more than ten counties in Suzhou and Songjiang, and the lives and property of millions of people depend on this line of seawalls for protection. Any negligence will lead to unimaginable disasters. In recent years, due to national unrest and financial exhaustion, repairs have been abandoned for a long time, resulting in collapses and landslides, with frequent alarms. In order to plan for the seawall project, Construction Director Shen Baixian was sent to inspect the four counties of Baotai-Changsong. The inspection has now been completed. According to the report, the seawalls of the four counties are full of sores. If all of them are repaired, it will cost no less than ten million yuan. Considering only the most urgent projects, the 1,000-zhang Baoshan Second Spring and Three Stone project requires 500,000 yuan, and the renovation of the original project requires 120,000 yuan. The 400-zhang Taicang Second Spring and Three Stone project requires 60,000 yuan. The 400-zhang Songjiang Second Spring and Three Stone project requires 200,000 yuan, and the renovation of the original project requires 50,000 yuan. The 400-zhang Changshu Seawall Beach Protection Project requires 200,000 yuan, and the renovation of the original project requires 50,000 yuan. The total construction cost for the four counties is 1.2 million yuan, which must be raised and started within the year, otherwise it will be impossible to defend against the autumn floods next year, and the consequences will be unimaginable. However, Jiangsu Province has suffered disasters for many years, and the treasury is exhausted, making it difficult to raise this large sum of money. This project is of great importance and cannot be delayed. Therefore, Chairman Chen Guofu of Jiangsu has submitted a report to the central government, requesting that funds be allocated from the national treasury for repair. If approved, it would be a great fortune for more than ten counties along the southeastern coast.

Consumption Status of Aquatic Products in this City in October: Totaling More Than 1.77 Million Yuan, Large Quantities of Salted Fish and Inferior Fish Imported 150

The Fishery Guidance Institute of this city yesterday released a detailed report to the Industry and Commerce News Agency on the import and consumption status of various aquatic products in this city in the previous month (October), as well as various statistics. According to the report, the total quantity of imported and consumed aquatic products in the previous month reached 98,751 dan and 82 jin, an increase of more than 32,000 dan, or about 48%, compared to September. The value reached 1,774,334 yuan, 5 jiao, and 6 fen, an increase of more than 755,600 yuan compared to September, or about 74%. Among them, the largest number was salted fish. On October 18, more than 36,000 dan of salted carp from the Sea Cucumber River (commonly known as Dongyang fish) were transported, with a value of more than 496,000 yuan. On the 23rd, more than 3,000 dan of Little Qingchuan transported from Canada to Shanghai were also worth more than 37,000 yuan. The sum of the two items accounts for more than the total increase in quantity. Although Japanese fishing vessels do not appear to have been imported, ice-preserved fish, such as yellow croaker, yellow flower, and shark, which were indirectly transported from Qingdao and disguised as domestic products, amounted to more than 20,000 yuan. As for various seafoods, such as sea cucumber and abalone transported from Hong Kong and other places to Shanghai, most of them are re-exported from Japan, in order to avoid the attention of the Chinese people. In addition, the average price of Lu fish in the previous month was slightly higher than in September, but the market price was very stable and there was no significant increase. The consumption statistics of various aquatic products are recorded below: 5,026 dan and 48 jin of fishing boats in this city, worth 50,610 yuan, 0 jiao, and 3 fen; 4,300 dan of fresh fish boats, worth 84,014 yuan and 74 fen; 10,298 dan of fresh barrel heads, worth 144,422 yuan and 90 fen; 53,139 dan and 04 jin of various salted fish, worth 703,383 yuan and 20 fen; 1,77 dan and 43 jin of various seafoods, worth 164,584 yuan, 5 jiao and 6 fen; 19,206 dan of freshwater fish, worth 54,321 yuan and 8 jiao; 4,899 dan and 43 jin of refrigerated fish, worth 77,757 yuan, 0 jiao and 9 fen; 111 dan and 44 jin of canned aquatic products, worth 6,344 yuan, 0 jiao and 4 fen.

National Radio Communication Status: China and the United Kingdom Have Agreed to Implement it on New Year's Day Next Year, Tibet, Qinghai, and Other Provinces are Actively Preparing 156

The Ministry of Communications believes that radio is very useful. In recent years, it has been expanding the installation of radio stations in the country and seeking communication with foreign countries. The following is a summary of the recent domestic and foreign radio communication status:

Domestic Radio Station Survey 157

The provinces that have already established radio stations include: (Jiangsu) Shanghai, Nanjing, Chongming, Qidong; (Zhejiang) Hangzhou, Dinghai, Ningbo, Kanmen, Shengxian; (Jiangxi) Nanchang; (Henan) Zhengzhou, Luoyang; (Anhui) Wuhu, Anqing (now abolished); (Shandong) Jinan, Qingdao, Yantai, Weihaiwei; (Hubei) Hankou, Shashi, Yichang, Wuchang; (Hebei) Beiping, Tianjin; (Hunan) Changsha; (Yunnan) Kunming can be relayed to all parts of Yunnan Province and Macau; (Sichuan) Chongqing, Chengdu, Wanxian, Xuzhou, the above four stations can be relayed to the entire Sichuan Province; (Guangdong and Guangxi) Guangzhou, Shantou can be relayed to all parts of Guangdong and Guangxi Provinces; (Fujian) Fuzhou, Xiamen; (Guizhou) Guiyang can be relayed to all parts of Guizhou Province.

Border Area is Preparing for Establishment 158

As for the border provinces, such as Xinjiang, Tibet, and Qinghai, the only means of communication they currently rely on is military radio stations. The equipment for commercial radio stations is still lacking. In order to complete the national radio route plan and develop border commerce and culture, the Ministry of Communications recruited more than 20 telegraphers who were willing to serve in the border areas and sent them to Xinjiang last month to prepare everything. They have now arrived in the provincial capital of Dihua, but due to political disputes in the province, they have been unable to implement the original plan. Once the province returns to normal, they can officially communicate. Tibet and Qinghai are also actively preparing, and communication will be realized soon.

International Communication Report 159

The Ministry of Transportation believes that international radio communication is closely related to enhancing relations between countries and promoting commerce. Therefore, it has been actively working to establish communication with various countries. Currently, formal communication has been established with the United States, Russia, France, the Netherlands, Germany, and other countries. As for the planned Sino-British communication, the construction of the new radio station and antenna tower in Zhenru is also being completed step by step. Two transmitters ordered from Britain have arrived in Shanghai, one of which has been assembled and is ready for use. The other one is expected to arrive in Shanghai within days for installation. Formal communication is scheduled to begin on New Year's Day next year.

Establishing a Telecommunications Manufacturing Factory 160

Furthermore, after the dissolution of the old Telecommunications Manufacturing Factory, the Ministry of Transportation notes that the supply of electrical materials to provinces across the country is being handled by the Electrical Machinery Manufacturing Factory of the Construction Committee. However, the output is insufficient to meet demand. The Ministry of Transportation now intends to establish a telecommunications manufacturing factory in Shanghai to remedy this situation. All plans have been finalized, and operations should begin soon once funding is secured.

Newspaper Reporters Association Holds Autumn General Meeting Yesterday; Initiates the Organization of a National General Association of Reporters; After the Meeting, a Dinner Party with a Raffle of Domestic Goods; An Unprecedented Grand Occasion with a Jovial Atmosphere 161

The Shanghai Newspaper Reporters Association held its autumn general meeting at the Daya Building on Fuzhou Road yesterday afternoon at 4:45 PM. More than 150 reporters from various newspapers attended. Representatives from the Municipal Party Committee, the Municipal Government, and the Social Affairs Bureau were also present to provide guidance. Several important association affairs were discussed. The meeting adjourned at 6:30 PM, followed by a dinner party with an impromptu raffle of domestic goods. Finally, a movie was screened. The event ended around 9:00 PM in a joyful atmosphere. The grand scale of the event was unprecedented for the association. Details are as follows:

Meeting Order: The meeting venue was set up in the east hall of the Daya Building, with the stage facing west. Above the stage hung a portrait of Sun Yat-sen and the national flag of the Kuomintang. To the left and right were the agenda and a list of staff members. The meeting began at 4:45 PM. The order of proceedings was as follows: (1) Opening of the meeting; (2) Election of two chairpersons by the general meeting; (3) All attendees stand at attention and bow three times to the national flag and Sun Yat-sen's portrait; (4) The chairperson respectfully reads Sun Yat-sen's will; (5) Three minutes of silence; (6) The chairperson delivers an opening speech; (7) Representatives from party and government organizations give instructions; (8) Reports; (9) Discussion of proposals; (10) Adjournment.

Meeting Staff: Presidium: Yan Duhe (jointly recommended by the supervisors and executive committee), Yu Kongwo, Qian Cangtian (jointly recommended by the executive committee); Qu Shaoyi, Jiang Zongdao (selected by the general meeting); Master of Ceremonies: Qian Hua; Secretaries: Jiang Jianhou, Sun Daosheng; Recorders: Wu Zhongyi, Yun Yiqun.

Chairperson's Address: After the chairpersons were elected, Qian Cangtian led the attendees in performing the proper ceremonial greetings. Then, Chairperson Yan Duhe delivered the opening speech, stating: "Our association's charter stipulates that a general meeting should be held twice a year, in spring and autumn. Since the spring general meeting, half a year has passed in an instant. Today, comrades, we gather together once again. Recalling the events of the past half-year, many feelings arise. From my personal perspective to each of you comrades, and to the entire association, there is a sense of shame. This is because the position of a newspaper reporter is closely related to the nation and society. Therefore, today, if newspaper reporters cannot contribute to the nation and society, it is due to the limitations of the environment. However, we do not shirk our responsibilities. Recalling the spring general meeting, we resolved to send a telegram to the generals in North China, urging them to strive to protect our national territory, and to express our condolences to Song Zheyuan, Guan Linzheng, and others who fought heroically against the enemy. But now, what has become of the territory of North China? We are not only humiliated by foreign powers but also facing drastic changes internally, sinking us further into a desperate situation. It is truly painful to speak of this. However, newspaper reporters take public opinion as their primary duty and serve as the voice of the people. They have a major responsibility to the nation and society and must not abandon their duties and progress due to temporary environmental constraints. This is what we should encourage each other to do. What is somewhat comforting is that the reporters of Shanghai, despite being in an unfavorable environment, can still unite and proceed on the right track. The membership of our association is also increasing daily. I hope that all members of this association will become more and more motivated, working hard despite the extremely difficult environment to fulfill the duties of a newspaper reporter."

Party and Government Instructions: After the chairperson delivered the opening speech, representatives from party and government organizations gave instructions: (1) Mao Yun, representative from the Municipal Party Committee, stated: "In a democratic country, sovereignty resides in the people. Only when the people pay attention to national affairs and exercise their powers can the nation and the people achieve prosperity. Therefore, education is the fundamental plan for the nation. Social education is closely related to the people and is extremely necessary. Gentlemen of this association, you bear a great responsibility. I hope that you will guide society based on the interests of the nation and the people, and especially pay attention to news concerning morals and customs, so as not to poison society. The future of the nation and society truly relies on you." (2) Zhang Yuanruo, representative from the Municipal Government, stated: "Newspaper reporters should self-discipline themselves with the words 'truth' and 'sincerity,' and uphold them consistently. Only then can they fulfill their mission in the era of enlightenment and lead society to progress day by day." (3) Zhou Hanmei, representative from the Social Affairs Bureau, stated: "The press is the leader of the people. Therefore, I hope that your association can take on the great mission of cultural movement to build a new China, so that the scattered culture can be unified."

Association Affairs Report: Next, Vice Chairperson Qu Shaoyi reported on association affairs, stating that at the spring general meeting, the total number of members was 199. One member died, five members withdrew, and 49 new members joined. The total number of members is now 242. (2) The number of meetings held by the Executive and Supervisory Committee, the expenditure of regular expenses, and the funding provided by various newspapers. Next, Sun Daosheng reported on the progress of collecting domestic goods for prizes and contacting for movie screenings, and expressed gratitude to various domestic goods manufacturers and the Educational Film Association and Promotion Office.

Discussion of Proposals: (1) This association should collect and purchase as many Chinese and foreign journalism books and newspapers as possible for members' reference. (Resolution) Passed. (2) Members of this association work diligently in various newspapers all day long and have no time to rest. Within a possible scope, travel groups should be organized to visit various places for sightseeing, to relax their minds and broaden their horizons. (Resolution) Passed. (3) This association intends to hire doctors of various Chinese and Western specialties to benefit the health of members and their families. (Resolution) Passed. (4) Increase the number of committee members. (Resolution) Passed in principle. The number will be determined at the next general meeting. (5) This association should compile a national newspaper yearbook. (Resolution) Passed. (6) The entire association should initiate preparations for a national general association of newspaper reporters. (Resolution) Contact local newspaper reporters associations to initiate preparations, and notify places where associations have not been established to organize them as soon as possible. (7) Petition the central government to abolish news censorship in the shortest possible time. (Resolution) Petition the central government to abolish it promptly. The meeting adjourned after the discussions.

Drawing Prizes: After the meeting adjourned, attendees immediately took their seats for the dinner party, which was divided into 15 tables. During the dinner, prizes donated by various domestic goods manufacturers were drawn. The names and quantities of the items were seen in yesterday's newspaper. The winners of the special prizes were: No. 1, Xu Chihen, won an electric fan; No. 2, Hu Yizang, won Zhanghua clothing material; No. 3, Xu Tianfang, won Meihua cheongsam material; No. 4, Jin Xiongbo, won a wall clock; No. 5, Zhu Mingxin, won a liquor stove; No. 6, Wang Jinqi; No. 7, Chen Xiliang, each won a Huafu felt hat. After the dinner, the Shanghai branch of the Chinese Educational Film Association and the National Educational Film Promotion Office voluntarily screened films. The association also agreed to provide voluntary screenings for any future social gatherings.
