The Truth About the Cricket Gambling Den is Fully Exposed; The Son of a Former Premier and a Bank Manager Were Both Involved; The Five People Who Failed to Appear on Bail Will Be Summoned by the Court on a Scheduled Date 167

Yongheng Bank on Ningbo Road leased its surplus rooms to Huaan Bank as a business premise. Huaan Bank's fourth floor had extra rooms, which were leased by the landlord to Lu Heshang to set up a cricket fighting gambling den. He gathered people who were into this activity and held intense competitions day and night, betting with money, with wins and losses amounting to thousands upon thousands. The matter came to the attention of the police. Last Wednesday, detectives were dispatched and arrested 77 gamblers and the person running the den on the spot. They were taken back to the police station along with the gambling tools and crickets, where they were placed on bail and detained separately. The next day, they were brought before the First Special District Local Court for interrogation and punishment, and were ordered to be released on bail. Five people failed to appear for questioning and will be summoned to the court again to investigate the details. This has already been reported in previous newspapers. Among the gamblers caught this time were descendants of officials and gentry, wealthy merchants, and magnates. Fearing that revealing their real names would not only result in a loss of face but also cause various disadvantages, they all concealed their true identities and fabricated false names. Now that most of the cases have been closed, and the matter has passed, the truth has gradually leaked out. According to insiders, two grandsons of Wang Wenshao, a former Premier in the Qing Dynasty, a nephew of Shen Jinjian, the former governor of Zhejiang Province, Chen Haiqiu, the current manager of Yongheng Bank, as well as Qiu Lao Jiu, a Mr. Ma, etc., were all among those arrested. Three or four of them were especially prominent. In addition, there were many others of a slightly lower rank. However, all of them arranged for relatives and friends to pay their bail in cash at the police station that night, without experiencing the taste of detention. The two grandsons of Wang Wenshao originally lived in Hangzhou. Upon learning that the gambling den was large in scale and the wins and losses were huge, they couldn't resist the temptation. They brought their invincible generals, which they had carefully trained, especially to Shanghai, hoping to return fully loaded with the generals' prowess. Who knew that the troops would suffer a setback, and both man and insect would be captured? Although the men were able to redeem themselves with money, the insects were confiscated by the authorities. The Wang brothers loved their insects as if they were their own lives. Suffering such a loss, they have returned to their hometown dejectedly. The five people who evaded the court appearance will continue to be summoned by the court next Thursday.

Robbers Sentenced Separately 168

Detectives Shen Binkui and Huang Fugen from the Hongkou Police Station previously arrested a large number of robbers, including Zhang Jinfa, Ye Afu, and Shen Jigui and Zhang Ahong, who were sentenced in another case by the Second Special Court, a total of nine people. One handgun and 48 bullets were confiscated. Investigation revealed that from August 13th to November 1st, these people, armed and in a gang, robbed the households of Li Kunxin at No. 6 Yuezhou Road, Fan Wangshi at No. 102 North Zhejiang Road, Chen Caoshi at No. 871 Yalu Road, Yang Zhicheng of Xielong Tobacco Company at No. 763 Niuzhuang Road, Cao Zhiyi at No. 68 North Suzhou Road, and others, amounting to more than 2,500 yuan. They were sent to the First Special District Court for interrogation and sentencing. Yesterday morning, Judge Xiao Xiefei presided over the Third Criminal Court and sentenced Ye Afu and Shen Jinyuan to ten years in prison, Zhang Jinbao to twelve years, Ye Rongyu to eight years, He Jifen to seven years and six months, Shen Jigui to seven years, Zhang Jinfa to five years, Zhang Ahong to four years and eight months, and Gu Genbao to six months. The number of days of detention before the sentence was determined was calculated at two days of detention equal to one day of imprisonment. The guns and bullets were confiscated. Xia Shutang, a Chinese detective from the Hongkou Police Station, previously arrested Jiang Xiaoqing, a Jiangbei native, at the Risheng Tea House on East Xihuaide Road for selling counterfeit banknotes. Fourteen five-yuan notes from the Bank of Communications, two ten-yuan notes from the Bank of China, and six five-yuan notes from the Dongshan Province were seized (altered waste notes from Zhang Zongchang's era). He was transferred to the First Special District Court for interrogation and detention. The other day, Judge Hua Yukui presided over the Third Criminal Court for further interrogation. Wang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated that the accomplices could not be arrested by changing the date, and that the manufacturing organization was difficult to investigate. He presented the counterfeit banknotes for inspection, stating that these counterfeit notes were indistinguishable from genuine ones. The defendant confessed that Zhao Zhengbiao, Liu Dezhang, Lu Wenguang, and Ma Demao, who were at large, asked him to sell them on their behalf for the first time. The court appointed lawyer Zheng Wenkai to defend the defendant. After further deliberation, the defendant was returned to detention, and the sentencing was scheduled for a later date.

Tang Zhezhi Sued for Ignoring Pawn Redemption 169

Tang Zhezhi, a Guangdong native residing at No. 77 Yuqingfang, North Sichuan Road, mortgaged seven shares of China International Sugar Company stock with a face value of 70,000 yuan to Hequn Business Co., Ltd. at No. 3 Hankou Road for 52,500 yuan in May of the previous year. Hequn found out that the sugar company had not yet started operating and that the stock was worthless, so they initially refused to accept it. Tang then turned to his fellow villagers Jian Qinshi, who resided at No. 736 Niuzhuang Road, and Ma Jiling from Hangzhou, who assumed joint and several guarantee responsibility. Hequn, considering that the two guarantors had a certain status, agreed to accept the mortgage and signed a contract specifying the repayment date. However, Tang failed to redeem the mortgage as agreed when the time came, owing a principal and interest balance of more than 67,245 yuan. Hequn repeatedly demanded payment but was ignored. The guarantors also failed to fulfill their guarantee obligations. Therefore, the company retained lawyer Shen Yuesheng to file a lawsuit in the First Special District Local Court against Tang and the two guarantors, Jian and Zhu, requesting that the three defendants be ordered to jointly and severally repay the debt. The company also stated that Tang Zhezhi had no ability to repay, and that the guarantors' whereabouts were uncertain. They requested that the court order a provisional execution at the time of judgment to avoid difficulties in future executions. Judge Peng has repeatedly held court hearings to investigate the matter and has concluded the investigation. The sentence was originally scheduled to be pronounced last Saturday, but due to certain points in the case that needed further examination, the sentence was not pronounced at that time. It is said that another hearing will be scheduled for further arguments before a judgment is rendered.

Defense Corps Intercepts Kidnappers 170

Chen Boying, a native of Pudong residing at No. 5 Jiderli, Caojiadu, currently works as a mechanic at the Shenxin Factory. Chen has a daughter named A'er, who is five years old. The day before yesterday morning, she was playing alone at the entrance of the house. Suddenly, a kidnapper named Gu Heshang used the lure of buying candy to kidnap A'er and flee without a trace. After his daughter disappeared, Chen searched everywhere but found nothing. Yesterday morning, the kidnapper Gu Heshang, leading the girl Chen A'er, was walking in Tushanwan, Shanghai West. He was spotted by Bi Jian, a member of the 10th Team of the Shanghai South District Defense Corps stationed there, who found his behavior suspicious. He went forward to question him. The kidnapper gave evasive answers. The team immediately took him for strict interrogation. According to his confession, his name was Gu Heshang, 31 years old, from Zhu Jiatang, Meijialongzhen South. He kidnapped the girl from Caojiadu at the house of a certain Mr. Jia. Last night, he stayed at a small inn in Baxianqiao. Today, he was entrusted to take her to the countryside, which was the truth. Based on the confession, the team immediately sent someone to search for the girl's father in Caojiadu. Chen Boying arrived, recognized her, and prepared a document to hand them over to the First Sub-station of the Sixth District of Xujiahui, which would then be transferred to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Major Fire on Huakang Road, Zhabei; More Than 50 Thatched Sheds Destroyed; Xia Sushi Suffers Burns to Shoulder and Arms 171

At 1:40 AM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out for unknown reasons at the thatched shed home of Xia Sushi, located at No. 119 along the road at the intersection of Huakang Road and Jinling Road in Zhabei. In an instant, flames broke through the roof. Since the west end of the site was Huakang Road, the north boundary was Jinling Road, and the southeast sides were adjacent to tiled houses, the nearby shops and residents panicked when the fire started. Fortunately, Qiu Weiyue, the police officer on duty at the post, arrived quickly after hearing the alarm. He urgently telephoned the fire brigade to report the fire. Fire trucks arrived to put out the fire, and the fire was extinguished at 2:20 AM. Nearby tiled houses were spared from catching fire, but all the more than 50 thatched sheds (housing more than 100 families) were completely destroyed. Afterwards, Police Officer Qiu arrested the arson suspects Wu Futang and Xia Sushi. After taking them back to the district, Wu Futang confessed that he was 30 years old and a native of Yancheng, making a living pulling rickshaws. He did not admit to starting the fire, saying that he was at the rickshaw company when the fire broke out, so he did not know where the fire came from, and so on. Xia Sushi, on the other hand, claimed to be 44 years old, also a native of Yancheng. The fire started in her house. She was already fast asleep with her three children when she was awakened by outsiders and escaped, but it was too late to put out the fire, so her arms were burned. She then showed her right arm, which was wrapped in paper from shoulder to wrist with broken skin and exposed flesh. However, she also did not admit to starting the fire, saying that she did not know who started the fire. Everyone said that she started the fire carelessly while cooking, but it was a wrongful accusation. The interrogating official examined the confessions and, considering that the case involved a fire, ordered that she be sent to the hospital for bandaging first, and then dispatched officers to investigate and verify the facts.

Careless Car Repair Shop Causes Injury 172

At around 4:00 PM yesterday, a fire suddenly broke out at the car repair shop at No. 3579, Lane 345, North Henan Road. Immediately, flames broke through the roof. The fire brigade arrived on the scene after hearing the alarm and made every effort to extinguish the fire. It took about half an hour to put it out. A total of four repair shops were destroyed. When the fire was raging, a woman escaped from the fire and was severely burned. Her family rushed her to the hospital for treatment.

Shop Assistant Arrested for Theft and Sent to Shanghai for Trial 173

The home of wealthy businessman Wei Tinghua, located at No. 51 Masnan Road in the French Concession, was recently robbed by shop assistant Yu Axiao (27 years old, Henglin Township, Changzhou) of silver utensils and fan ornaments worth more than 1,000 yuan, which were pawned to foreigners. When Wei discovered this and began investigating, Yu fled without a trace. Wei reported the matter to the French police and requested an investigation. Detectives Zhou Shizhang and Bao Bingquan discovered that Yu had fled back to his hometown. They reported this to the police chief, who in turn requested the court to prepare a document and dispatch it to the Wu County Public Security Bureau in Changzhou, requesting their assistance in arresting Yu. Yu was arrested and transferred to Shanghai. He was sent to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court the day before yesterday morning. Lawyer Yuan Jiahuang from the police station presented the case, stating that the police station had not yet investigated the case or recovered the stolen goods. He requested that the defendant be detained temporarily and that the case be investigated and brought to trial at a later date. Detective Bao then reported the process of arresting the defendant. Judge Wu Fanglian verified the report, briefly questioned the defendant, and then ordered the defendant to be returned to detention and questioned again on the 29th.

Selling Smuggled Cigarettes Leads to Fine 174

Tongmaoxiang Tobacco and Paper Shop, located at No. 46 on the front side of the West New Bridge in the French Concession, has recently been mixing smuggled, counterfeit Zhongnan and Fairy cigarettes with their retail sales. This was discovered by the French Concession Investigation Office of the Tobacco and Cigarette Unified Tax Bureau of the Ministry of Finance. The day before yesterday, West Detective U Yau led detectives Zhou Baosheng and Zhao Chengen to the shop to search. They seized 620 Zhongnan brand cigarettes and 600 fake Fairy brand cigarettes. They then brought the manager, Zhang Zhongming (25 years old, local), to the police station and transferred him to the Eighth Criminal Court of the Second Special District Court. Judge Wu Fanglian interrogated him. Lawyer Gu Shouxu from the police station first presented the case, filing charges based on the Regulations on the Collection of Unified Tax on Tobacco and Cigarettes and the Regulations on Penalties for Smuggling. He also presented the cigarettes as evidence. The defendant Zhang Zhongming confessed that a broker brought the cigarettes to sell, 1,400 Zhongnan brand cigarettes and 2,000 Fairy brand cigarettes. He dared to sell them because he did not know they were smuggled goods. After examining the confession, the court immediately pronounced its verdict, fining Zhang Zhongming 30 yuan for selling smuggled cigarettes and confiscating the smuggled cigarettes seized.

Peddler Commits Suicide by Poison in Hotel 176

Zhou Yusun, a native of Shaoxing, 30 years old, residing at No. 320 Hartung Road, was a peddler. Recently, due to a shortage of capital, he stopped doing business. The night before last, he rented a room at the Ping'an Small Hotel at No. 253 at the intersection of Pingjili Road and Lafayette Road in the French Concession. The next morning, the tea boy Chen Shuangfu (35 years old, native of Suzhou) knocked on the door to urge Zhou to get up, but there was no response after calling for a long time. He tried to open the door and went inside to check. He found that Zhou had already died in bed. He reported the matter to the French police, who dispatched officers to investigate. The cause of death was unclear, and there were no family members. The body was immediately transported to the mortuary of the Tongren Fuyuan branch. The Second Special Court was notified the same day, and the coroner determined that the deceased died of illness. He ordered the body to be handed over to Tongren Fuyuan Hall for photography and burial. Later, the deceased's younger brother, Zhou Yangsheng, learned of the death, rushed to the scene, signed a statement, and took the body away for coffining and burial.

In recent years, the society's affairs have been flourishing, and Ms. Dong's contribution to its support and planning has been significant. She has served as the director of the Women's Department and other positions in the society. She was 81 years old. She was usually in good health. The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated that there were clouds around Shandong, and there would be fog in the morning. The wind was coming from the northeast. Throughout the Yangtze River basin, the wind was gentle and undirected. In the coastal area south of Ma'an Island, the sky was cloudy or overcast, with localized rain. Its center was within 120 miles of the intersection of 18 degrees north latitude and 115 degrees east longitude at 2:00 PM, proceeding very slowly, sometimes stopping. The wind force was unknown. Starting Next Semester, Middle Schools in Other Provinces and Jiangsu Province Will Waive Tuition and Accommodation Fees. Additional Education Fees Will Be Collected Starting This Winter. Schools Will Continue to Charge Fees as Usual This Semester 188

In order to reduce the burden on students and provide relief to impoverished children, enabling them to receive secondary education free of charge, the Jiangsu Provincial Government has resolved to waive tuition and accommodation fees for all provincial middle schools throughout the province. The provincial government has ordered all counties to implement this measure starting in the next semester of this year. The details are as follows:

Amount of Reduction

The tuition, accommodation, and other fees collected by provincial secondary schools throughout Jiangsu Province amount to a total of 200,000 yuan per year. The Jiangsu Provincial Education Budget allocates this 200,000 yuan annually as administrative revenue to cover regular expenses. Since the Jiangsu Provincial Government passed the resolution to waive tuition and accommodation fees for all secondary schools throughout the province, the school administrative fee income item in the education budget will be reduced by 200,000 yuan.

Method of Compensation

The method of compensation is to add 20 cents to each stone of grain in the provincial tax revenue. The annual grain tax in Jiangsu Province is approximately 1.5 million stones. Due to crop failures and defaults by the people, it is not possible to collect the full amount uniformly. After discounts, each stone is calculated at 20 cents, which can yield 200,000 yuan to compensate for the waived tuition and accommodation fees.

Source of Grain Tax

The grain tax method was first established by the Advisory Bureau in the Xinhai year. In the first year of the Republic of China, the Provincial Assembly resolved that the grain tax would be 5 yuan per stone, divided into provincial and county taxes, with the province receiving 4 yuan and the county receiving 1 yuan. For silver, the tax was 2 yuan and 5 cents per tael, with the province receiving 1 yuan and 75 cents and the county receiving 30 cents. Since the establishment of the Jiangsu Education Funding Management Office, the education fees have been separated. Of the 4 yuan provincial tax per stone of grain, the Finance Department collects 2 yuan and 6 dimes, and the education fees collect 1 yuan and 4 dimes. Of the 1 yuan and 75 cents provincial tax per tael of silver, the Finance Department collects 1 yuan and 28 cents, and the education fees collect 47 cents.

Winter Grain Tax Collection

Since the Jiangsu Provincial Government passed the resolution to compensate for the waived tuition and accommodation fees for secondary schools, starting with the collection of this year's grain tax, of the 4 yuan provincial tax per stone of grain, the Finance Department will collect 2 yuan and 4 dimes, a decrease of 2 dimes compared to before, and the education fees will collect 1 yuan and 6 dimes, an increase of 2 dimes compared to before. Although the education fees for grain have increased by 2 dimes per stone, the actual burden on the people has not increased at all. The Jiangsu Provincial Government has repeatedly ordered all counties to remit 2 dimes per stone for education fees starting with this year's grain tax.

Waiver of Tuition and Accommodation

The waiver of tuition and accommodation fees for all provincial secondary schools throughout the province will be implemented uniformly starting in the next semester of this year (i.e., next spring). This semester, because the grain taxes are just beginning to be collected, the schools will continue to charge fees as usual in the autumn. This measure is entirely to provide relief to impoverished children throughout the province and enable them to receive secondary education free of charge.

Order Issued by the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department: Amended Measures for Collecting Student Fees in Provincial Middle Schools. Provisional Measures for Awarding and Assisting Impoverished Students Also Amended and Promulgated. 189

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department issued a general order regarding the waiver of accommodation fees for provincial middle schools in the next semester: It has been found that the measures for collecting student fees in provincial secondary schools were previously formulated by this department and circulated for implementation, and have been followed for many years. Now that the Provincial Government Committee has resolved to waive tuition and accommodation fees for all provincial schools starting in the second semester of the 22nd year of the Republic of China, other fees such as library and physical education fees should also be re-established based on the regulations of the Ministry of Education and considering the students' family economic burden and assessment methods. All previously established measures for collecting student fees in secondary schools have been revised separately. In addition to submitting them to the Provincial Government for review and record, and requesting the Ministry of Education to file for record, the revised measures are also issued separately to the principals of the schools, ordering them to comply with the revised measures for collecting student fees from the second semester of the 22nd year of the Republic of China and to ensure strict compliance. This order... Amended Provisional Measures for Collecting Student Fees in Jiangsu Provincial Secondary Schools.

Article 1: Provincial secondary schools shall strictly comply with these measures when collecting student fees.

Article 2: The student fees collected by provincial secondary schools each semester are specified separately as follows: (1) Physical Education Fee: Middle schools and vocational schools shall charge 1 to 2 yuan per student per semester; normal school students are exempt. (2) Library Fee: Middle schools and vocational schools shall charge 1 yuan per student per semester; normal school students are exempt. (3) Lecture Notes Fee: For all secondary schools, junior high schools shall pre-pay 1 yuan per student per semester, and senior high schools shall pre-pay 2 yuan per student per semester. (4) Experimental Materials Fee: For all secondary schools, junior high schools shall pre-pay 1 yuan per student per semester, and senior high schools shall pre-pay 2 yuan per student per semester. Vocational schools may increase the amount as appropriate. The funds for the preceding three and four items are handled on an agency basis and are settled once per semester. Surpluses are refunded, and deficiencies are supplemented. (Note) If the school prepares medical supplies for student use, it may charge a medical fee with approval.

Article 3: Each school shall use all student fees collected for the specified purposes and shall not divert them to other uses. Separate accounts must be established, and at the end of each semester, a report of receipts and expenditures, along with supporting documents, shall be submitted to the department for review and shall be posted publicly within the school.

Article 4: When new students enroll in middle schools and vocational schools, they shall pre-pay a 5-yuan deposit for compensation for losses. When normal school students enroll, they shall pay a 10-yuan guarantee deposit. Both shall be refunded upon graduation. If public property is damaged and compensation is required, the amount shall be deducted accordingly. Normal school students who leave school midway shall not have their guarantee deposit refunded.

Article 5: The following fees shall be handled according to the following regulations if handled by the school on behalf of the students: (1) Meal Fee: Except for normal school students who are exempt, all other secondary schools shall pre-pay the fee at the beginning of the semester. The amount shall be determined by the school according to the local cost of living and shall be settled once at the end of the semester. Surpluses shall be refunded, and deficiencies shall be supplemented according to the actual expenditure. It is even more appropriate if the school can guide students to organize a cooperative to handle it. (2) Uniform Fee: Uniform materials must use domestic products. Each time the school collects the fee from students in advance, it shall not exceed 12 yuan. If it is necessary to prepare winter coats, the amount may be increased as appropriate.

Article 6: In addition to the above regulations, provincial secondary schools shall not collect any other fees from students. If there are special circumstances where it is necessary to charge students fees temporarily, a special report shall be submitted to the Education Department for approval before implementation.

Article 7: These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department and shall be reported to the Provincial Government for referral to the Ministry of Education for record.

Amended Provisional Measures for Awarding and Assisting Impoverished Students 190

The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department also ordered: It has been found that this department previously formulated the Jiangsu Provincial Secondary Schools Provisional Measures for Awarding and Assisting Impoverished Students in order to award and assist impoverished students in provincial secondary schools, and circulated it for implementation and submitted it to the Provincial Government for approval and record. Now, in order to reduce the burden on the families of impoverished students and add scholarships to increase the educational opportunities for impoverished students, all previously established award measures have been revised. In addition to submitting them to the Provincial Government for review and record, and requesting the Ministry of Education to file for record, the revised measures are also issued separately to the principals of the schools, ordering them to comply with the revised measures starting in the second semester of the 22nd year of the Republic of China. This order…

Amended Provisional Measures for Awarding and Assisting Impoverished Students in Jiangsu Provincial Secondary Schools 191

Article 1: The Jiangsu Provincial Education Department has established scholarships specifically for awarding and assisting impoverished students in provincial secondary schools.

Article 2: Students in provincial secondary schools who are genuinely impoverished and meet one of the following requirements shall be awarded and assisted separately: A. Those with excellent conduct, sound physique, and an average academic score of 80 or above, with all subjects passing, shall be exempt from library and physical education fees for the next semester and shall be awarded 20 yuan for books, meals, and other expenses; normal school students shall be awarded 10 yuan for books. B. Those with excellent conduct, sound physique, and an average academic score of 70 or above, with all subjects passing, shall be exempt from library and physical education fees for the next semester and shall be awarded 10 yuan for books, meals, and other expenses; normal school students shall be awarded 5 yuan for books. C. Those with excellent conduct, sound physique, and no absences in one semester, with an average academic score of passing, shall be exempt from library and physical education fees for the next semester and shall be awarded 5 yuan for books; normal school students shall not receive additional awards.

Article 3: The number of scholarships for each category is stipulated as follows: Category A shall not exceed 2% of the total number of students; Category B shall not exceed 3% of the total number of students; Category C shall not exceed 4% of the total number of students. If the number of qualified students exceeds the specified quota, the school affairs meeting shall determine the acceptance or rejection based on the degree of poverty separately and, if necessary, may include them in the next category of scholarships.

Article 4: Students requesting exemptions shall submit an application prepared by their parents before the start of the semester, along with a guarantee provided by their guarantor at the time of enrollment, to the principal for review. Upon receiving the aforementioned request, the principal shall immediately conduct a detailed and accurate investigation, submit it to the school affairs meeting for decision, and then report it to the Education Department for approval and handling, and shall post it publicly within the school.

Article 5: If it is discovered that any student receiving awards or assistance has made false declarations, in addition to recovering the fees that have been waived and awarded, the principal and guarantor shall be jointly and severally liable.

Article 6: The library and physical education fees exempted by each school shall be offset against the corresponding revenue items, and the scholarship funds shall be requested from the Education Department each semester.

Article 7: These measures shall be promulgated and implemented by the Jiangsu Provincial Education Department and shall be reported to the Provincial Government for referral to the Ministry of Education for record.

China: Standards for Boy Scout Specialty Qualification Training (3) 192

(27) Fishing 1. Able to knit a fishing net; 2. Knows various fishing methods such as seine netting, cast netting, drag netting, angling, and spearfishing; 3. Knows the methods of catching shrimp, crabs, eels, etc.; 4. Knows the breeding of fish-eating ducks and fishing methods; 5. Able to achieve considerable success using three or more catching methods; 6. Has basic knowledge of fish farming.

(28) Meteorology 1. Able to create a meteorological report for two or more months; 2. Able to predict weather through natural phenomena such as solar and lunar halos, auroras, and rainbows, as well as insect signals and bird calls; 3. Familiar with weather report charts from observatories; 4. Must be familiar with storm warning signals; 5. Understands the relationship between meteorology and crops.

(29) Navigation 1. Knows navigation rules and various navigational marks and ship light signals; 2. Able to read nautical charts; 3. Knows how to use a sounding line; 4. Able to estimate a ship's position using cross bearings; 5. Able to sail a sailboat and operate a lifeboat; 6. Able to use life-saving equipment; 7. Must have one month or more of sailing experience and a detailed report; 8. Must be familiar with various signs of customs, tides, wind, rain, and hurricane warnings; 9. Must have the qualifications for a swimming specialty badge.

(30) Animal Husbandry 1. Knows the general situation of animal husbandry in China and other countries; 2. Knows the essentials of animal husbandry; 3. Able to raise one type each of poultry and livestock and provide a detailed report of the rearing process; 4. Knows new methods and benefits of raising dairy cows and chickens; 5. Knows first aid for poultry and livestock diseases.

(31) Zoology 1. Knows the ten major phyla of the animal kingdom, and can provide an example of an animal from each, describing its physiological form and relationship to human life; 2. Able to identify forty species of birds and animals and know the life and habits of more than twenty species; 3. Able to draw four types of protozoa using a microscope and provide an experimental report, explaining class, movement, nutrition, and reproductive functions; 4. Able to distinguish more than twenty different bird calls; 5. Able to identify more than five types of bird and animal feathers and footprints; 6. Knows how to identify and protect beneficial birds.

(32) Afforestation 1. Knows the forest production areas of China and the benefits of afforestation for the people's livelihood; 2. Knows afforestation and cultivation methods; 3. Knows the methods of planting, grafting, irrigating, pruning, and protecting trees; 4. Able to identify various trees by their appearance; 5. Able to distinguish age and wood quality by tree rings; 6. Knows the methods of logging and transportation; 7. Has personally planted more than ten trees.

(33) Commerce 1. Knows the current state of commerce in China, an overview of tariffs, and the general trends of international commerce; 2. Knows the general principles of commercial practice and store organization and management; 3. Knows the general principles of banking, insurance, and exchange transactions; 4. Able to write commercial correspondence and keep commercial books; 5. Possesses general commercial knowledge and understands the importance of commercial ethics; 6. Knows the company regulations and regulations regarding trademark registration and product patents.

(34) Chinese Martial Arts 1. Has practiced martial arts for more than one year; 2. Able to perform four unarmed boxing routines and one set of weapon routines; 3. Able to perform one wooden staff routine; 4. Knows the schools of Chinese martial arts and the advantages of each school; 5. Able to teach two or more people and achieve excellent results.

Local News: Public Funeral Held Yesterday Morning for Four Boy Scouts Who Died in the January 28th Incident 193

Luo Yunxiang, Ying Wenda, Bao Zhengwu, and Mao Weixiang, four martyrs who were members of the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce Boy Scout Troop (50th Troop) and died for the country in the January 28th Incident, have not had their remains recovered. To commemorate their heroic spirits, the troop specially consulted with the Shanghai Public Cemetery, which donated a burial plot. Jinshan Stoneworks constructed a cenotaph at half price, using Jinshan stone. The construction of the first phase of the tomb base has been completed. Yesterday morning, the troop held a ceremony at the troop headquarters in front of the Four Martyrs Memorial for placing the symbolic garments into the coffin. The families of the martyrs personally placed the garments, and senior troop members helped cover the coffin and boarded the troop's military vehicle, which drove to the Shanghai Public Cemetery. A burial and public memorial ceremony was then held, with solemn and grand rites, expressing deep mourning.

Yesterday's Group A Football Match: Donghua and Western Police Tie, 1-1; No Score in the First Half; Zhou Guangzhong Opens the Scoring; New Lineup Fought Well 201

Yesterday (Sunday) afternoon at 3:00 PM, Donghua and Western Police played the first week of the Group A round-robin match at Yiyuan Stadium. Donghua was the champion of the previous season. This encounter with the fiercely combative Western Police naturally attracted many fans. Looking at the overall situation, the moments of brilliance were evident. Donghua was not diminished by the absence of three injured key players from last week's match against Youyou. Zhou Guangzhong, Shen Guanlan from Jiaotong University, and Yu Shunzhang from Fudan University joined to assist. The coordination was satisfactory. Therefore, in a dramatic match, thanks to the efforts of the players, a tie was achieved. There were more than 6,000 spectators. In the last two minutes, Lu Zhongen was penalized and sent off for arguing with the referee.

Donghua Team:

Lu Zhongen

Feng Yunyou Guan Xun'an

Tu Kaiyuan Shen Guanlan Wu Youliang

Wan Xianghua Zhou Guangzhong Yu Shunzhang Chen Hongguang Jia Youliang

Western Police Team:

Bros

Turner Hughes

Heresh Xu Fales

Wogensheng De Fei Sheng Lijieke Bote

Starting the Competition 202

Three bells rang, and Donghua arrived first and tested their footwork. Then, Western Police also arrived. Referee Bot blew his whistle, and Western Police chose the field. Donghua kicked off first, but the ball was intercepted by Zha Xu and sent to the front. The five Western Police forwards fiercely attacked the goal. Several offsides were in vain. After about ten minutes, Chen Hongguang got the ball and made a long pass. Jia Youliang had a one-on-one opportunity to directly attack the enemy's line, but the ball was blocked and kicked out by the Western Police goalkeeper. Donghua's midfielder Shen Guanlan assisted in all directions and was generally satisfactory. Jia Youliang had two corner kicks, and Wan Xianghua made several passes, all of which were well-placed, but unfortunately, there was no one to shoot, and the opportunities were missed.

Dangerous Moments 203

After thirty minutes, the area in front of the Donghua goal was full of enemy figures. Fortunately, Feng and Guan consolidated their defense. In addition, Lu Zhongen caught the high ball and kicked it out to defuse the danger. At forty minutes, Western Police's Turner fouled thirty yards to the left of the goal. Wu Youliang took the free kick, and Yu Shunzhang made a beautiful shot, but it went through the crossbar and missed, which was a great pity. Zha Xu snatched the ball from the middle and sent it high to the right corner. The ball was already out of bounds, but the referee missed it. Fortunately, it was saved by Feng Yunyou. The first half ended, and both sides had achieved nothing.

After Lemon Time 204

After switching sides, both sides fought even harder due to their eagerness to win, and their actions were somewhat rough. Donghua's goalkeeper Lu Zhongen was penalized for walking four steps with the ball (commonly known as "shooting the fence"). De Fei lofted the ball over the crossbar. With the crisis gone, Donghua's forwards bravely charged into the Western Police territory, like a surging tide. Fales blocked too eagerly, resulting in an injury, but he recovered quickly. Shen Guanlan made a long pass to Wan Xianghua. Wan curved the ball from the sideline in front of the Western Police goal. Zhou Guangzhong calmly flicked the ball into the goal, opening the scoring. Donghua took the lead with one goal.

Returning the Goal 205

After losing this goal, the Western Police all paled in comparison. They quickly rallied and made a vigorous counterattack. Lu Zhongen was overwhelmed. Finally, De Fei scored a goal, tying the score. The difference between the two goals was only five or six minutes. Donghua then sent troops from the border, but the Western Police goalkeeper saved the ball from the crowd. Heresh passed to Bote, who made a solo run but missed. In the forty-third minute, Lu Zhongen was dismissed from the field by the referee for arguing with the referee about corner kicks and out-of-bounds balls. Tu Kaiyuan substituted him. Fortunately, time had run out. Ah Tu kicked the ball once, and the game ended in a 1-1 draw.

Shanghai Women's Basketball Association: Qiangdong Wins Group B Championship; 34-21 Over Liangliang; Xu Wenying Performs Excellently; Finals Tonight 206

Qiangdong and Liangliang are the two outstanding teams in the Shanghai Women's Basketball Group B. They met last night in a crucial match for the championship. Both teams were fully focused on competing. The five hundred and ten female spectators who came to appreciate the game were also very excited, cheering and shouting to support their respective teams. After the contest, Liangliang started strong but then faded, while Qiangdong continued their efforts, turning defeat into victory, winning with a score of 34-21, and winning the Group B Women's Basketball Championship. In another game, Guanghua and Shangzhong showed improved skills day by day and gave a good performance. As a result, Guanghua won with a score of 32-15. The details of the Qiangdong and Liangliang game are recorded below.

Liangliang Takes the Lead: The two teams lined up, and Liangliang's three forwards immediately launched a fierce attack. Zhu Hefeng, with the support of her teammates, was like a phoenix soaring in the sky. Qiangdong struggled to gain momentum, relying only on Xu Wenying's free throw for one point. Afterwards, Liangliang continued to dominate. Although Qiangdong was unwilling to be outdone, they were relatively less effective. In the first quarter, Liangliang led with 9-4.

Tied Score: After a brief break, the game resumed. The Qiangdong ladies were greatly encouraged and determined to fight to the death. They worked hard to attack, but still struggled to score, while Zhu and Li scored one after another, taking a commanding lead with 15-4. At this point, the audience was disappointed with Qiangdong. However, the players on the field were not discouraged and calmly responded. Xu Wenying and Xue Jinghua worked well together, and the score gradually narrowed. As the first half ended, Xu's center shot from the left corner, creating a 16-16 tie.

Comeback: After a ten-minute break, the competition resumed. Both teams struggled even harder in this tense situation. Miss Xue scored a basket in the paint, taking the lead. Xu Wenying's free throws were successful, further advancing their progress. The Liangliang players were in a state of collapse, blocking fiercely and committing frequent fouls, causing the defenders to tremble. This gave Qiangdong an opportunity to attack. At the end of the third quarter, Qiangdong took the lead with 26-18.

Qiangdong Wins the Championship: In the fourth quarter, Qiangdong took advantage of their momentum and became more powerful. Xu Wenying, like a butterfly flitting among flowers, scored three consecutive baskets. Knowing that the situation was critical, the Liangliang players fought bravely to the death, but their eagerness to win led to recklessness, resulting in a complete collapse. As time ran out, Qiangdong won with a score of 34-21, winning the championship.

International Triangular Track and Field Meet; Baihong Wins the Championship; Second Place to Russian Community, Third Place to Japanese Community; Next Session Scheduled for April Next Year 209

The international track and field competition between the Baihong, Russian Community, and Japanese Community groups continued yesterday with three events: discus throw, triple jump, and distance relay. The Japanese Community won two events, while Baihong only won the discus throw. Chen Baoqiu's score of 34.03 meters was quite good. In the overall score, Baihong won the championship with 90 points, the Russian Community was second with 52 points, and the Japanese Community was third with 43 points. The details are recorded below.

Discus Throw 210

The participants included three from the Japanese Community, three from the Russian Community, and two from Baihong. Chen Tieniu did not bring his spiked shoes and wore long pants and leather shoes. He threw the discus casually and surprisingly well. He threw over 30 meters on his first attempt. By his third attempt, he spun and threw 34.03 meters. After that, he did not dare to exert himself due to a hand injury, and could not make further progress. Biao and Guangtian were eliminated in the preliminary round. Glashan had a tall stature, but unfortunately, his throwing technique was not good, and he fell to second place. Japan's Takahashi and Russia's Brokov did not exceed 30 meters. First place: Chen Baoqiu (Baihong), 34.03 meters; Second place: Brokov (Russian Community), 33.72 meters; Third place: Glirim (Russian Community), 31.85 meters; Fourth place: Fu Baolu (Baihong), 31.13 meters.

Triple Jump 211

Xiao Dinghua, who had not participated in the triple jump for a long time, happily took the field yesterday to boost the team's morale. As expected, the veteran was a classic and not easily eliminated. He jumped 12.82 meters on his first jump, only 16 centimeters short of Komatsu. On his second jump, Komatsu showed his colors, and the measurement result was 13.43 meters. Lao Xiao made slight progress until his sixth jump. The results were the same as Brokov. The final decision (one more jump) was that Komatsu was slightly better. First place: Komatsu (Japanese Community), 13.43 meters; Second place: Xiao Dinghua (Baihong), 12.88 meters; Third place: Deguchi (Japanese Community), 12.26 meters; Fourth place: Brokov (Russian Community), 12.26 meters.

Relay 212

First leg, 200 meters: Chen Baolin started in an excellent position, but at 120 meters, Japan's Okamoto overtook Bao Lin by one step and passed the baton. Second leg, 400 meters: Liu Fukang tried to catch up with Japan's Nagashi, but his leg cramped after entering the turn, and Nagashi still caught up. Third leg: Wu Zijing ran swiftly with the baton, competing fiercely with Japan's Nishinai. At 700 meters, Nishinai could not hold on, but Russia's Gu De阔夫 started to chase from 20 meters behind, showing great potential to catch up. Fourth leg, 200 meters: Xue Jianqiu relied on a quick baton exchange and took the lead all the way to the finish line. The time was 4 minutes and 3 seconds. Russia's Da Lie夫chen阔 closely followed, but fell behind by one shoulder. Japan's third runner collapsed at the finish line, and the situation was over. The track yesterday was 300 meters per lap.

Soochow Law School - Three Ball Teams Embark on Expedition to Suzhou and Wuxi 220

The Law School of Soochow University in this city places great emphasis on sports. In order to arouse the students' interest in sports and to connect with the Suzhou Liberal Arts College, the Student Union of the school has decided to send three teams, volleyball, basketball, and women's basketball, to Suzhou for competitions on the 1st of next month, and to Wuxi for competitions on the 2nd. Zhao Shouchang and Ren Xianqun will lead the teams. They will return to Shanghai on the 3rd. Many of the members of the school's volleyball and basketball teams are well-known players, such as Li Yongxi, Wu Guoxiong, and Zhao Congyan. They have attended the National Games before. This expedition to Suzhou and Wuxi is expected to yield good results. Dr. Sun Xiaolou, the academic dean of the school, will hold a farewell banquet for them in the coming days, and the entire school will hold a grand send-off.

Published every Saturday, Issue 50

The Reasons for the Flourishing of Banking Business in Shanghai by Wei Youfei 221

I.

In the past two years, there has been a clear trend in Shanghai, which is the flourishing of the banking business. It goes without saying that Beijing Road and Ningbo Road are regarded as the Wall Street of Shanghai. Even areas such as Sichuan Road and Xinzha Road to the north, Jing'an Temple Road to the west, and the area around Eight Immortals Bridge all show a tendency for banks to be everywhere. Is this phenomenon due to an overabundance of financial capital, or is it an urgent need of the commercial society?

The newly established banks generally have small capital, with a maximum of 500,000 to 1 million yuan. Their power is not strong, and their business items are largely similar. The establishment of so many banks, reflecting the current market situation, will naturally make people wonder if their business focus will tend to conflict. This is the motivation for this article.

The reason for the flourishing of the banking business in Shanghai, simply put, is the concentration of floating capital in Shanghai. Because Shanghai is a city, a special city. Since the government established its capital in Nanjing, its economic position has become increasingly important. Import and export transactions must go through Shanghai, funds must come to Shanghai, the focus of securities is on Shanghai, the market price of exchange is on Shanghai, and the executives of the mint and the central bank are still in Shanghai. This alone makes it the forefront of the concentration of banking businesses. If we analyze the reasons for the concentration of floating capital, then:

Agricultural reasons: wealth originates from industry and agriculture. China is an agricultural country, with the agricultural population accounting for 80% of the total population. The majority of these farmers rely on agricultural products to maintain their livelihoods. Years of famine have led to rural bankruptcy, increasing the number of unemployed in rural areas and endangering rural security. The bourgeoisie, who have always lived in the countryside, are not only seeing a decline in their wealth due to the decline of the countryside, but also fear for the safety of their property. Moreover, as problems arise in public security, government and military expenditures must increase. Due to the remote location of rural areas, the burden on these limited assets of the bourgeoisie is bound to increase. On the income side, it is declining; on the expenditure side, there is a growing trend. This is an important reason for driving the bourgeoisie away from the countryside and into the Shanghai group. Moving to Shanghai not only allows them to avoid the heavy and choose the light, but also, because of Shanghai's special circumstances, their wealth and lives can be worry-free. The continuation of this situation will further promote the decline of the countryside, making the two sides extremely divergent.

Industrial reasons: China has no real industry. Everything is struggling under the aggression of capitalist imperialism. The so-called national industries, silk factories and cotton mills, are all in a state of distress. Even the raw materials they use are almost entirely dependent on others. In recent years, the decline of the countryside and the reduction of agricultural products have caused pain to both farmers and industry. The farmer produces, and the industrialist consumes. Because of the difficulty of making a living, the general purchasing power is low. Coupled with the layers of exploitation by the capitalist powers nearby, self-operated factories are doomed once they suffer misfortune. Because of the blows to industry, capitalists, who were originally going to devote themselves to industrial advancement, now, in view of the situation, have to turn this capital into floating capital. Bankruptcies occur, and those who have not yet gone bankrupt, seeing the reality, stop their efforts. As a result, finance becomes stagnant. Since the beginning of this year, the daily market interest rate has been hovering between 5 and 6%, which is enough to show that the movement of funds is directionless, which is rare in the past.

II.

How is this floating capital used? It is impossible to open factories. As for running businesses, the widespread famine and banditry make most merchants frown. While they wait for opportunities, they want to place their funds in a place where they can be active. At the same time, they want to maintain their position as business leaders and expand their influence. Only running financial businesses can meet these two conditions.

The powers of shareholders in stores and companies are limited, and there are fewer people who can manage them. As for old-fashioned stores, shareholders have no direct way to increase their status. Therefore, only financial businesses have these two characteristics. When funds are needed, they can find ways to borrow from their own banks, on the one hand to generate interest, and on the other hand to prevent the funds from stagnating. Moreover, at the same time, the potential growth of financial power is the backing of business and reputation.

There are two ways to run a financial business: one is to run a native bank, and the other is to run a modern bank. However, running a native bank is more difficult than running a modern bank. The reason is easy to explain. Native banks are old-fashioned organizations, and shareholders have unlimited liability, which is a heavy responsibility, while the shareholders' powers are small. This is one reason. Secondly, the shareholders of a native bank must have real strength as a backing, especially during periods of financial alert, the strength of the shareholders is needed to cope with the situation. As such, the shares of native bank shareholders cannot be too fragmented. Usually, there are only ten shares, and the number of shareholders is at most four or five. These four or five people must not only have substantial assets and reputation, but also have a kind of "turning around" ability. Therefore, being a shareholder of a native bank is easy to become burdened for capitalists. Banks are not like this. Several hundred yuan per shareholder, combined with many small shareholders, makes the position of the major shareholders particularly solid. Major shareholders of banks have a greater hope of being appointed as directors, which can give them a strong influence. If they see that the market is good, they can further develop their own strengths and engage in a certain business. If funds are insufficient, they can turn to their own bank for turnover, which is probably more fluid than before the bank was opened. Therefore, native banks are a collection of large entrepreneurs, while banks are a combination of many small entrepreneurs to support and develop a large enterprise.

At this time, using floating capital to run a bank is a way for capitalists to find a way out for their capital. Their own position can of course be increased, they can also obtain considerable profits, and they can also place many unemployed people. It is indeed the most appropriate way to deal with the situation.

III.

From the above, given that the reality of the economic society is in this form, from where do financial businesses extract their profits? The biggest goal of financial businesses is to take in funds and use them. The usual principle is to make loans. However, in the current situation, industry and commerce need loans, but financial businesses are wary and dare not take risks lightly, thus creating a stalemate. There are two ways out for the banking industry in Shanghai:

The first is to operate in public debt. When the state is in financial distress, it often uses issuing public debt as the only way out. We know that the interest on public debt is more generous than ordinary loans, and we also know that the issuer of public debt is the government, and its payment of principal and interest is guaranteed, which is enough to reassure the general financial capitalists. This is especially better than ordinary loans. Therefore, the government uses this as a way to plan government affairs, and banks also use this as the only method of investment. Banking businesses are also afraid that the profits will not be widespread, so they collect fragmented deposits and operate in public debt in bulk. The bank benefits on one side, and the government loses on the other. The source of government finance is the people, so the bank's profits are secretly taken from the people. Industrial and commercial businesses that actually need loans do not receive any real benefits. This is a distorted development, which is not conducive to the future of enterprises.

The second is to operate in real estate. When the countryside goes bankrupt, the wealthy and floating capital all gather in Shanghai by coincidence. The population of foreign residents tends to increase, and the population of the concessions expands, thus promoting the soaring of land prices in Shanghai. Moreover, due to the competition among capitalists, the momentum of land price increases is accelerated. Financial businesses use this point to engage in the purchase of real estate in addition to focusing on public debt. Due to the banks' frantic purchases, the rise in real estate accelerates, and financial capitalists are able to sit back and enjoy the profits during this soaring period. Financial capitalists collect deposits in small amounts from depositors, increase their capital strength, and are able to implement their large-scale profit-making plans.

Merchants naturally aim to make profits, and financial businesses cannot find a way out outside of merchants. However, the biggest goal of financial capitalists is definitely not to increase their own profits, and their source comes from the use of distorted exploitation. Their main business relies on the fact that both the government and the people are in a disadvantageous position, and the financial capitalists' strength in underwriting public debt is so strong that they can often look down on everything. The latter is especially enough to make financial turnover inflexible, leading to a stagnant situation. When will our financial capitalists be able to turn to the right path?

Women's Savings and National Economy by Li Junsi 222

Today, the fierce competition in the banking industry is an undeniable fact. They spare no effort in attracting deposits, with many different names and all sorts of tricks. For example, education savings, old-age savings, children's savings, etc., as well as increasing interest rates, priority savings, and various advertisements are all methods of attracting deposits. In all fairness, if this kind of competition is purely business competition and does not contain any elements of mutual exclusion, slander, or jealousy, then the bank will deliberately improve and strive to serve the society because of competition, and the society can also use it freely and obtain a lot of convenience. However, if we carefully observe the banking industry, we can find a shortcoming, that is, banks lack sufficient promotion of women's savings, and opportunities to serve women are still rare. If we say that there are 400 million compatriots in our country, then 200 million of them are female compatriots. Taking a step back, we assume that only a portion of the 200 million female compatriots are in a privileged position and have the ability to save, then every little helps, and these countless weak funds gathered together can become a strong new force, making a great contribution to the real economy. Who can say that this effect is weak! Unfortunately, the banking industry in our country has not taken this into consideration.

According to the usual situation, in today's male-centered society, women's occupations are still in their infancy. Most women are still managing household affairs and relying on their husbands' supplies. However, women's ability to save is not lacking. Undoubtedly, every woman is the manager of every family. She has the authority to control the family economy and is endowed with the special privilege of managing the family finances. In the daily family expenses, if she saves a little bit, then it is very easy to save up. And the husband always gives his wife some money every month, and women mostly cherish money very much and are reluctant to spend it. In this situation, it can be seen that women's savings power is indeed very rich. As for some women who are engaged in occupations, needless to say, they have a considerable income every month, and they do not bear much economic responsibility in the family, so their savings power is even stronger. However, banks not only lack promotion of women's savings, but also rarely have equipment suitable for women's savings. The underdevelopment of women's savings has created two phenomena in society: one is the extreme consumer, that is, the so-called modern woman. In their minds, there is no concept of saving, only vanity occupies their hearts, so their clothing, decorations, and gestures are all extravagant, so consumption, simply put, is extravagant, which is of course to be expected. The other is the absolute conservative. They lack sufficient knowledge of investment, and they have a skeptical attitude towards banks and are a little distrustful, thinking that hiding it themselves is the most appropriate way to dispose of their private savings. Among women, most are conservative, but there are also not a few who are open-minded. Strictly speaking, the former is certainly fostering the social custom of extravagance and increasing social consumption. Although consumption is also production, it reduces the national economic power. The latter puts useful funds into prison, preventing them from circulating in society. In terms of industry and commerce, it invisibly reduces an economic power. In short, both are major obstacles on the path of developing the national economy. Therefore, from the standpoint of the bank, it should make every effort to promote thrift and savings to consumers, and inform them that savings are not only related to the happiness of an individual's life, but also a responsibility that every citizen should fulfill. Because the bank has the mission of promoting thrift and changing the social custom of extravagance, it should also vigorously persuade conservatives to make them deeply understand what kind of financial service the bank is providing to the society, and to put their savings into the bank. Undoubtedly, this kind of persuasion is also an obligation that the bank should fulfill. However, most of the current banks are deluded by the immediate small profits, and ignore their great mission. Therefore, we feel that the underdevelopment of women's savings, in addition to the fact that most women do not approach banks, the banks themselves cannot escape the blame.

In the future, the banking industry should not ignore women's savings any more. In addition to allocating a portion of its resources to engage in publicity work, within the possible range, banks should set up a women's savings department and employ female tellers to specialize in this matter in order to get closer to the general public of women. In this way, most women will naturally be willing to interact with banks, and the further development of bank business is also an inevitable trend. We want to believe that after the development of women's savings, it will be very easy to use this fund to help most women who lack the ability to save and make them produce the ability to save as well. Furthermore, to revitalize industry and help the countryside, why not declare it? Therefore, in the years when the level of national economy is declining and social phenomena are abnormal, banks should shift their gaze and pay considerable attention to women's savings.

A Comprehensive View of the Economic Panic by Chen Honggen 223

(1) Introduction. "Panic" is a modern term, a byproduct of the Industrial Revolution, and has only been noticed since the 19th century. Because of China's industrial backwardness, no one cared about it in the past. However, in recent years, domestic industries have developed considerably. According to the results of various surveys, the number of workers is as follows:

Agricultural workers...87,218,000 (Shen Bao Yearbook)

Factory workers...1,445,000 (China Labor Yearbook)

Miners...2,289,000 (Torgasheff)

Transportation workers...129,073 (Ministry of Railways, Ministry of Communications, etc.)

Handicraft workers...2,850,000 (China Labor Yearbook)

Total: 93,931,073

Based on this, the number of workers in our country is also quite considerable. Once production loses its adjustment, its impact on people's livelihoods will be enormous. Moreover, since the world panic in 1929, a widespread state of unemployment has been created, and our country has also been significantly affected. The study of the panic problem cannot be delayed. However, the content of the panic is complex and complicated, and cannot be fully explained in a few words. Various countries have written special books on it. Limited by space, this article can only make a general statement on the causes, development steps, impact, and relief policies of the panic.

(2) The Cause of the Panic. The reason for the panic is the imbalance between production and consumption. Since the introduction of machine production, the factory system has emerged, adopting precise division of labor and using large amounts of capital, raw materials, and labor to produce large quantities of goods. Can this large quantity of goods be confirmed to meet the needs of society? The answer is not necessarily. Producers often do not understand the market situation and often guess. As a result, production and consumption gradually become separated, and the amount of production often exceeds or falls short of the amount of social consumption. The former will inevitably lead to overproduction, while the latter will form low consumption power (UnderConsumption). As a result, prices will inevitably fall, commodities will be in a state of stagnation, credit will be destroyed, and finance will be in chaos. The entire economic society will be disturbed, and panic will be formed.

(3) The Nature of the Panic and the Procedure of Development. (1) Nature. Panic has two special characteristics: (A) Cyclicality... A panic occurs approximately every ten years. This is indeed a strange thing. Some interpreters believe that it is due to the action of sunspots, or that it is caused by the circulation of credit. However, since 1870, the interval has changed slightly, either seven years or five years, but there is no doubt that it has cyclicality. (B) Intermittent Severity (Double Population)... Panic has another important characteristic that is easily overlooked, that is, every time it occurs, a severe one will occur. An "X" in the table below indicates a severe panic, especially the one in 1929, which was unprecedented:

X 1818 1825

X 1837 1847

X 1857 X 1873

1884 X 1893

1903 X 1907

1920 X 1929 (Most Severe)

(2) Development Procedure. The occurrence of panic has its specific steps, which can be roughly divided into four periods!

(A) Prosperity Period. Before the panic occurs, the economic society will show a lively phenomenon. First, prices increase due to a surge in demand, and new enterprises will inevitably emerge. Old enterprises, tempted by high profits, will also expand greatly, and everyone will embrace an optimistic attitude. During this era, the need for labor will also increase. Because of the need for capital, the credit system will inevitably develop, and interest rates will inevitably exceed the horizontal line. (B) Financial Panic Period. As mentioned earlier, the stability of the economic society depends entirely on its ability to maintain a balanced development. However, since prices are expensive, production enterprises have expanded greatly, and cash has been absorbed by producers. The circulation of currency will inevitably be insufficient. In order to expand capital or increase currency, various banks or companies absorb deposits or issue banknotes excessively. Once a run on the bank or a withdrawal event occurs, and the bank or company cannot cope, it will inevitably lead to the closure of its business, forming a currency panic (Monetory Crisis). (The bankruptcy of John Cook & Co in the United States in 1873 and KnickerBocker & Co in 1907 can be used as examples.) Although producers are willing to continue to absorb capital, investors rush to recover capital, so production enterprises will inevitably stagnate, and prices will fall day by day. (D) Severe Panic Period. Once prices have fallen, and producers are unable to absorb capital as a remedy, the result will inevitably be factory closures. Once factories have been closed, the capital previously used for production will enter a state of rest and be flooded in the market, and its interest rates will turn to lower. (C) Revival Era. After production enterprises have been shut down, the quantity of goods will inevitably decrease day by day, and the needs of society cannot be reduced with it. With a small amount of goods to supply a large amount of demand, their prices will gradually rise. Entrepreneurs, seeing that there are profits to be made, will invest again. This cycle repeats itself, completing a panic cycle.

(4) The Change of Prices and the Panic. The basic cause of the panic is overproduction, and its external manifestation is through the rise and fall of prices. Therefore, to understand the dynamic state of the panic, we must first study the procedure of price changes in detail. According to the facts, the rise and fall of various prices do not necessarily occur at the same time, and their degree and main materials vary. The procedure is listed below:

(A) Government bonds, stocks, etc... This type of price is the most sensitive, and any slight stimulation or change from the outside will be expressed. For example, during the war last year, the price of government bonds soared as soon as it was relatively peaceful, and fell immediately once it was tense. (B) Wholesale Prices. The speed of their rise and fall is also very large. For example, if external demand increases slightly, their price will rise, and vice versa. (C) Retail Prices. Their speed is not as fast as wholesale prices, because their relationship with prices is more indirect. (D) Wages. Their rise and fall depend entirely on wholesale and retail prices (the reason will be explained later). (E) Long-term Contracts. This type of rise and fall is extremely slow, because it is limited by time (such as rent, land rent, etc.).

(5) The Relationship Between Panic and Unemployment. What is the relationship between panic and unemployment? It is not difficult for us to obtain it from the procedure of price changes in the previous section, which is briefly described below:

(A) Period of Rising Prices. According to the above procedure, producers benefit first when prices rise, and retail prices then rise. The cost of living for workers will inevitably increase, and their inherent wages will not be able to cover expenses, and they will further demand an increase. Because they can make profits, capitalists are also happy to share part of the profits to increase the remuneration of workers. Therefore, both labor and capital have benefits during this period. (B) Period of Falling Prices. When prices fall, wholesale prices bear the brunt, so capitalists suffer first, followed by a fall in retail prices, and a fall in wages follows retail prices. At first glance, this procedure seems to be quite beneficial to workers, as they can enjoy cheap goods. However, this advantage is only temporary, because capitalists have no profit to make, they will inevitably stop their production business, and workers will become unemployed. Therefore, a fall in prices also symbolizes a premonition of unemployment, and overproduction is the main cause of falling prices and panic. The relationship between panic and unemployment can be seen from this.

(6) The Relief of Panic. The relief of panic can be observed from two aspects: one is to formulate general relief laws, and the other is to establish rescue measures for panic unemployment.

(A) General Relief Measures. (1) Laissez-faire Policy. The theories of optimistic economists and Adam Smith can also be used to relieve panic, because the nature of the panic is cyclical, similar to the operation of celestial bodies, which cannot be changed by human power. Furthermore, in terms of human nature, once prices fall, producers will automatically stop production, and prices will inevitably rise again after a long time. Furthermore, those with sharp eyes can take precautions in advance. Therefore, panic is actually a kind of natural elimination, which is necessary and indispensable. However, according to the facts, the arrival of panic causes the wise and the foolish to perish together, indiscriminately. Moreover, panic is only temporary. If this short period of misfortune can be avoided, wouldn't it be of great benefit to mankind? Therefore, this method cannot be considered good. (2) Control and Limit Production Enterprises. The main cause of panic is overproduction, so it is appropriate to restrain it in a negative way, promote the Cartel movement, avoid competition and conflict between enterprises, and then it can be agreed upon prices, share profits equally, and distribute sales routes without leading to a phenomenon of surplus. (3) Encourage Consumption. On the one hand, panic is due to overproduction, but on the other hand, it is due to low consumption capacity, so we should try to increase the people's consumption capacity. The methods are nothing more than (A) reducing prices, (B) paying prices in installments, and (C) promoting cooperative consumption, etc. (4) Increase import duties on foreign goods and implement dumping policies at home and abroad. The former can reduce the source of goods, and the latter can give domestic goods the opportunity to sell well. (5) Set the price of currency. The expansion of production depends on a large amount of currency. With the abundance of currency, producers can borrow at low interest rates to expand their production. At the same time, the expansion of credit currency also has the danger of disrupting finance. Therefore, it is appropriate to limit the amount of currency in circulation to increase interest rates, so that production enterprises will not expand excessively, and panic will also be reduced.

(B) Relief Measures for Panic Unemployment. (1) Determine the Production Plan. Capitalists should first consider the steps of their production, so that they can develop in an average way, so as to avoid concentrating in a certain period, resulting in overproduction in that period, which will lead to labor unemployment in the later period. (2) Shorten Working Hours. One effect is that workers will not suffer from idleness or overwork, and the other is that unemployed workers will also have the opportunity to work. For example, in the past, a worker worked twelve hours a day, while at the same time, a worker had no work to do. If we now order the former to work seven hours, then the latter can also get considerable work. (3) Improve Vocational Education. So that workers can adapt to a variety of jobs, even if a certain production business is shut down due to overproduction, they can still participate in other production businesses. (4) Organize Well-Functioning Employment Agencies. To seek a way out for unemployed workers, this business is not very developed in our country. The 20th National Congress passed a worker unemployment relief bill, one of which was to establish employment agencies in various cities. Later, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce also promulgated regulations on employment agencies. The employment agencies that have been established now are in Nanjing, Peiping, Shanghai, Tianjin, Hankou, Qingdao, Guangzhou, Jinan and other places. (5) Charitable Business. Subsidies for unemployed workers. (6) Unemployment Insurance. This system originated in the city of Ghent in Belgium. Therefore, it is named Ghent System. It has been promoted in various countries since then, and it has been quite effective. It once declined during the war, but it has developed greatly again after the war. This system has not yet been implemented extensively in our country, and the government should vigorously promote it.

The above is a general description of the relationship of the panic. Since the recent economic depression, the world has been panicked and at a loss. If we can carefully analyze it, we will naturally be able to find its clues and it will not be difficult to provide relief. The Technocracy School of Economics in the United States is aimed at preventing panic and rationalizing production. If their theory can be implemented, wouldn't it be the greatest happiness for mankind?

Letter from Readers 224

Dear Sir/Madam, I read the article "Relief for Rural Bankruptcy and the Pawnshop Industry" by Xie Ejun in the Economics Weekly on page 5 of your newspaper on the 13th. It describes the current rural situation in great detail, and I deeply admire it. However, there are three points that are slightly different from the facts regarding our bank's plan to set up an agricultural warehouse in Qingyang, Jiangyin. Please correct them to avoid doubts in all circles. (1) Name. According to the iron peasants, they originally relied on pawnshops to pledge items to borrow funds for turnover. Last year, pawnshops closed down, and the peasants' economy had no way to circulate. Therefore, the local party and government agencies and local people jointly applied to our bank to go to the pawnshop site to run a warehouse, which was named "Qingchang Shangji Agricultural Warehouse," not an item mortgage office. (2) Types of Collateral. According to local customs, the bulk of the mortgage is food and cloth. Our bank only accepts these two types as the standard, and other clothing items are not mortgaged. This type of mortgage is only to facilitate the peasants' temporary economy and retain the opportunity to wait for the price to sell out, so as to avoid the loss of the low price at that time. Therefore, there is no need for an excessively long period of six months, and it is not an imitation of the Shanghai small pawnshop method. (3) Interest Rate. Our bank stipulates that the maximum is one point, plus an insurance fee of four points for the warehouse rent, totaling one point and four mills, not one point and six mills. The above three points should be included in the "Letter from Readers" column, so that readers can understand the development of the Qingyang Shangji Agricultural Warehouse, and I will be very grateful. Sincerely yours, Agricultural Cooperation Loan Department of Shanghai Commercial & Savings Bank.
