Securities: Last Week's Bond Market in a Storm; The Minbian Crisis Was Serious, and Many Bulls Fled; The Market Result Was Unanimously Like a Waterfall 226

Last week, from November 20th to 25th, the market at the China Commercial Securities Exchange was stormy and violent, even more so than the previous week. The Minbian Crisis had moved from serious to burst, which was the first act of the Minbian Crisis. The subsequent situation will depend on whether the Guizhou and Guangxi provinces support it, whether the central Guangdong province assists the central government in suppressing Fujian, whether the war is inevitable, and its location, and whether welcoming Hu can be achieved. All kinds of situations are enough to sway the rise and fall of the government bond market. The situation is unusually complicated, and the news is also changing rapidly, which is the second act. At present, it is still in the brewing period of the second act, and there are many changes in the future. However, with the central government's military strength and the current isolated situation in Fujian, it should not be difficult to quell it immediately. The government bond market, which has been shocked by this, has a future like a boat sailing in a huge wave, and its panic is inevitable. Last week, due to busy trading every day, only three rounds were done. On Monday, the situation in Fujian suddenly became serious, and it was known that the burst could not be avoided. Large households sold out one after another. Although the 11th slightly covered the short position, it was already a drop in the bucket. Market prices fell sharply by several dimes to one yuan and three dimes. On Tuesday, the Minbian Crisis actually broke out and declared independence. Large households sold out, and retail bulls came out of the cage, which was even more panic. Market prices plummeted, and most had already found new low prices, which were about one yuan less to two yuan and three or four dimes compared to the previous day. However, at the close of the market, the surface had slightly seen short covering. On Wednesday, the new changes in the Minbian Crisis and the central government's severe handling of it, and Guangdong Province's cooperation with the central government, the market price suddenly rebounded, and the rebound was very strong. Large households such as the 47th and 54th bought in, and the total increase was several dimes to one yuan and two or three dimes. Jinzhang rose sharply by two yuan, which was the rebound at the end of the first act of the Minbian Crisis. On Thursday, the first round inherited the rise of the previous day, and the remaining momentum was still strong, rising another half yuan or so. After that, rumors arose again, and it became tired again, and there was still no vigor. On Friday, rumors about the Minbian Crisis were rampant again, and the bulls came out of the cage, and those who changed positions were extremely eager. Market prices fell sharply again, and many varieties saw low prices again, mostly about one yuan or so and one yuan and eight dimes. Saturday was the last day of this month's futures. At first, the situation was slightly settled due to Guangdong's use of troops against Fujian. In the first and second rounds, there was a rebound. In the afternoon, the news was bad again, and it turned down again. The trend was that Guangdong Province had no intention of sending troops, and Zhejiang Province became serious again, and the future was still difficult to be optimistic. American Cotton: Limited Transactions Last Week 229

New York, November 24th, New York telegraphed the cotton market situation for the week, saying that the spot cotton market this week was mixed, and transactions were limited. A small amount of arbitrage sales were absorbed by the industry. In addition, transactions were limited to some squaring and the advance liquidation of the December period. The currency debate has disturbed the popularity of speculators and shaken the trust in the gold purchase plan. Because of the belief in the expansion theory, some of the buyers who bought in have now liquidated, which is probably the reason. Japanese merchants bought in when prices fell. According to Washington news, farmers in the South who hold term cotton contracts will soon be able to receive 4 points per pound of惜款. As a result, 200,000 to 400,000 bales of cotton were handed over to cotton farmers to pay part of the cotton field rent, so that there would not be pressure to sell in large quantities at a price of less than one dime per pound.

Spring and Autumn

Ten "Don'ts" and Ten "Musts" for Body Protection Exercise 231

— Xiao Diren

Little friends! Isn't our body more important than anything else? Yes, right? Then, how should we protect it? Now, children in Soviet Russia have very good ways to protect their own bodies. They do not exercise their bodies through sports, nor do they take tonics to nourish their bodies. What they do are things we usually don't pay attention to! Now, I will translate them and introduce them below:

(1) Don't eat cigarettes, alcohol, and chili peppers; (2) Don't eat rotten food.

(3) Don't drink raw water; (4) Don't put your fingers in your mouth.

(5) Don't urinate or defecate indiscriminately; (6) Don't spit carelessly.

(7) Don't masturbate; (8) Don't rub your eyes with your fingers.

(9) Don't eat food sold in the open air; (10) Don't put urine buckets in the bedroom.

(1) The house must be cleaned; (2) Brush your teeth and bathe every day.

(3) Change clothes often; (4) Often [trim] nails.

(5) Kill mosquitoes; (6) Kill flies.

(7) Keep the windows of the house open; (8) Always wash your hands clean.

(9) Clean public places; (10) Practice getting up early.

There are a total of twenty items here, divided into ten "Don'ts" and ten "Musts". Therefore, they collectively call this the Ten "Don'ts" and Ten "Musts" Body Protection Exercise.

Little friends! This is very beneficial to our bodies, learn it!

The People Regard Food as Heaven 232

— Yan Gou

I went to the countryside to attend a wedding banquet. Although it wasn't "three days before and four days after", it lasted for four days. The first day is called "Xia Zhuo" (lower table). Originally, it meant that the pork, lamb, chicken, and duck needed for the wedding day, and the leftovers that were not elegant, such as the internal organs and offal, were eaten by relatives on the day before. Therefore, it is called Xia Zhuo. But now it's different. The dishes served are more abundant and better than on the wedding day. On the wedding day, there is no need to say much. Naturally, all three meals are big pieces of meat, big fish, and big bowls of wine. The next day is "Nuan Fang" (warming the bridal chamber). The guests give a gift and ask for several miscellaneous things, making noise for most of the night. This meal is similar to Xia Zhuo, or even better. The fourth day is thanking the accountant. Although it is not a large-scale invitation, close relatives and friends are also included. Therefore, eating is the most important issue for a wedding. There are even cases where the guests are unhappy because the host is stingy, the hospitality is inadequate, or the supply is insufficient, which shows the importance of eating.

Originally, since Suiren (a legendary figure who invented fire) had the troubles of music and marriage, eating was indispensable. However, this kind of eating is not beneficial to either side. On the host's side, a lot of money is spent. On the guest's side, sudden overeating may be harmful to the body. However, people generally believe that this is necessary to show its grandness. The more people eat, the bigger the face; the better the dishes, the wider the scene. Even the newly married bride must prepare more festive fruits to deal with the embarrassment of making fun of the bridal chamber. It is often heard that the guests are criticizing the bride's inadequacy, as if missing a handful of melon seeds or a cigarette would be a major flaw in the bride. "The people regard food as heaven." This can be seen here!

Eating a little more at a wedding banquet is still a happy thing, but having to eat for two or three days at a funeral is even more extravagant and inappropriate. I often go to funerals, pay my respects a few times, have a meal, wipe my mouth, and leave, and I don't even understand what's going on. But many families holding funerals are worried that not enough people are eating, and only a few tables are sitting sparsely in a large hall, which is quite unsightly.

Random Talk about Cartoons 233

— Qian Yun's writing, Lian Liang's drawing

丨Production Cooperation丨

My old man is one of the rickshaw pullers in the city, trained in the skill of earning a living, with two muddy legs; and indeed, through wind, rain, and snow, he has a body of copper and bones.

Mom also goes out early and returns late, sewing pants, mending socks, fair trade with Zhang San and Li Si, without deceiving the old or young!

The son is young, although he cannot develop the family business: but throughout the day, he picks up cigarette butts, sweeps up garbage, small gains make a big supplement, similar to general production.

Regarding the problem of the son's wife, it is said that he is very close to Little Shunzi, the daughter of the woman who empties the chamber pot next door.

Old San, who sells fried dough sticks, said he wants to be a matchmaker.

Making Do 234

— Qian Zuizhu

"Chinese people should use Chinese goods"

A large slogan caught Mr. Zhang's eye in a startling way.

"Of course, this is a national duty," Mr. Zhang thought.

"Ah!" Mr. Zhang thought, "This shop assistant is so muddled. This is Shanghai, not the three northeastern provinces, I'm afraid no one would be willing to run on the street wearing purple calico trousers and a jacket."

"This year is the Year of National Goods, we are especially offering discounts. Sir, please make do and try it, we will slowly improve," the shop assistant used his means of attracting customers.

Mr. Zhang, after all, was conquered by the clever business acumen, and took a bolt of Du cloth back. At the same time, he also brought back a question: "Why not teach 'goods to accommodate people' and instead 'people go to accommodate goods'?"

When leaving the market, the large slogan "Chinese people should use Chinese goods" once again caught Mr. Zhang's eye. Mr. Zhang suddenly understood!

1. In a shoe store

"My leather shoes are old, I should buy a pair. But where are the national leather shoes?"

Peeking and looking around, Mr. Zhang searched for shoe stores all over the street. "These are British leather, I don't want them. These are Japanese goods, I don't want them. I want to buy a pair of genuine Chinese leather shoes." Mr. Zhang requested this in a shoe store. "Yes, yes, purely Chinese leather shoes, but the style is a bit worse." The shop assistant busily found a pair of black leather shoes for Mr. Zhang.

"Are these Chinese goods? Why are they so ugly, how much?" After repeated scrutiny, Mr. Zhang reluctantly asked the price. "Four yuan and eighty cents," the shop assistant murmured. "Don't dislike them for being ugly, they are sturdy goods," he added.

"Isn't the British leather one written as four yuan and twenty cents? Why is the rough cowhide one more expensive?"

"This is a national product," the shop assistant said carefully, bringing a mysterious smile.

"Don't you have any better ones?"

"This is the best national product, if you want better, unless it's smuggled goods."

"Alright! I have no choice but to make do," Mr. Zhang paid the price of four yuan and eighty cents in "making do".

2. In the National Cloth Market

"Sir, this is famous Du cloth made from Chinese raw materials and Chinese manufacturing. Would you like to buy some?"

"Isn't this purple calico? Are there other colors? The width is also too narrow."

"Sir, this is the most popular national cloth sold in the three northeastern provinces, very strong..."

Fourth Company Commander of the Northeast 235

— Zhang Henshui

Chapter 19: Desiring to leave yet not, they recall past events in the same car; Half crying, half laughing, she leans on the pillow in a sick and decaying autumn

While he was hesitating, Ji Zhi could see his expression, so he said: There is a waiting room inside, shall we go there to sit and talk? Guizhi stopped, stared at his face for a while, blinked her eyelids, and then smiled slightly; Where is Second Master going? Ji Zhi said; Naturally to Haidian. The two spoke. He had already walked into the waiting room. Because it was still early, there was no one in the room, Guizhi didn't know why, but her face turned red again. Walking to the door of the room, she hesitated for a while, acting as if she wanted to enter but didn't. Ji Zhi first sat on a long chair, seeing Guizhi's hesitant look, he also stood up, smiled faintly and said; It doesn't matter. This waiting room does not distinguish between men and women, everyone is waiting for the train here. Guizhi thought to herself that if she didn't go in, it would make Ji Zhi look bad, so she walked in generously and sat down. Ji Zhi slowly took out a cigarette and matches from his body, slowly smoked it, and slowly puffed out two mouthfuls of smoke, without making a sound. Guizhi sat there, pulling at her clothes, and coughed a few times, before sitting down again. After Ji Zhi puffed out a few mouthfuls of smoke, he thought of a key sentence. He laughed and said; Miss, we are not as familiar as we were before as neighbors, now we are much more estranged. Guizhi smiled, but did not answer his words. Ji Zhi said; Friends are like this, being together every day, feelings will naturally get better. If we don't see each other for a long time, even good feelings will be lost. Guizhi smiled and said; The feelings of friends are always the feelings of friends, seeing each other every day is just like that, not seeing each other for ten years is just like that. Ji Zhi said; That's right, seeing each other every day is just like that, but thinking about the past, it seems that our feelings are more than just those of friends. When he said this, he glanced at Guizhi, to see what her expression was like? (250)

Bedside Notes 236

— Zhu Lu

In the few days after the Beginning of Winter, I suffered from overwork, and in terms of work, although I worked hard, it was impossible to not seek merit, and even seeking to avoid fault was impossible. Therefore, I couldn't help but feel pain in my spirit. In addition, at this time, lake crabs were on the market, full of fat and yellow, just right, I indulged my appetite, but it caused the old symptoms of coughing up blood. When I was seventeen years old, I had coughed up blood once, and later, when Yu'er died prematurely, it happened again. However, both times I only coughed up a few mouthfuls, slept for a few days, and took some medicines such as "Yijingcao", and it gradually stopped. This time, however, it was particularly fierce. Every day, I coughed up a full teacup of fresh blood. The traditional Chinese medicine decoctions were ineffective, and the Western medicine skin needles were ineffective even after two injections. For two consecutive days, I coughed up four cups of fresh blood. At that time, my wife was so frightened that she lost her soul. I also couldn't help but feel terrified. Death, for my body that has suffered so much, if I were to die in one breath, it would be a great relief. However, as a poor couple with no savings, I had to stand up and work hard every day. If I didn't work for a day, problems would arise. Although blood was being coughed up cup by cup, my mind was still very clear. Looking at the bright red blood, various thoughts arose. Thinking about the future, thinking about the various possibilities after death, it was unbearable to imagine. Fortunately, on the third day, a Western medicine intravenous injection caused me to break out in a hot sweat all over my body, and the bleeding stopped. However, after three days without eating, my ears were ringing and I was dizzy, and I was exhausted.

I am an unemployed person, relying on my pen for a living, month after month of hard work. I use the manuscript fees written by my pen to maintain the family expenses of two people; so it is also miserable, usually wearing cloth clothes and eating simple meals, I already feel very difficult. My family's living expenses are measured according to income, so I always try my best to save money wherever possible; clothing is not to be discussed, and in terms of diet, I also try my best to economize, but after this coughing up blood, for the sake of nourishment, I eat cod liver oil, chicken essence, eggs, soy milk, etc. every day. In terms of dishes, I also eat pig trotters and fatty ducks, enjoying a good appetite, restoring the enjoyment of a young master. But a low-ranking scholar actually enjoying the good fortune of a rich man is too humorous. But the doctor instructed me to obey strongly, and I could only temporarily ignore the economic problems of the future. "Cod liver oil" is said to be the most effective for nourishing lung diseases. However, pure cod liver oil is so fishy and oily that I can't eat it with my poor appetite. Milky white cod liver oil is also not easy to eat. The cod liver oil I eat is malt essence cod liver oil. However, in the domestic Dali brand malt essence cod liver oil, that layer of pure cod liver oil still floats on the malt essence, and the fishy and oily smell still exists. "Halibut Cod Liver Oil," the taste is delicious, but a bottle of cod liver oil costs three yuan and forty cents, which can only be eaten for half a month. For me, who has economic difficulties, I really want to eat it but can't afford it. After this coughing up blood, my dear friend Mr. Cheng Xiaoqing taught me a method of self-made malt essence cod liver oil. The method is very easy, and the value is particularly cheap. Although the taste is not as good as "Halibut", it is much better than Dali brand cod liver oil. I dare not keep it a secret, so I write it to tell my fellow sufferers.

The method is very easy. First, take two-thirds of malt essence (ie, maltose, commonly known as pure sugar). Add half a portion of clear water and cook over a gentle fire for twenty minutes. While the sugar is boiling, use a stick to mix the water, and then pour it into another container; let it cool for five minutes first, and then pour in one-third of the cod liver oil, and stir evenly as much as possible. You must wait until the sugar is solidified and cooled before stopping. When it is made, add some fruit essence, and the cod liver oil will be fragrant and delicious. To put it bluntly, this method is very easy, but there is a small trick, that is, when adding cod liver oil, you must wait for the sugar to cool for five minutes before adding it; otherwise, if you pour it in while it is hot, no matter how you stir it, the oil will float on top, and the sugar will settle at the bottom, and it will never mix well. Moreover, this self-made cod liver oil, five pounds of pure cod liver oil, plus ten pounds of malt essence, and two pounds of clear water, can make a full seventeen pounds of malt essence cod liver oil, and its value is only about four yuan, which is really cheaper than any tonic!

Mr. Zhou Shoujuan heard that I was coughing up blood and came to see me, and also passed on a prescription. That prescription was passed down from Mr. Xie Pengfei, a friend in Shanghai. It is said to be very effective in treating lung diseases, and the procedure is also very simple. The method is: first take a section of old lotus root, cut off the lid, add 70% rock sugar to the lotus root holes, put the lid back on, and bury it vertically in rice. After a week, then take out the lotus root, at that time the lotus root will be cooked softly, and the rock sugar in the lotus root holes will also be turned into sugar juice, pour it out and drink it, the sweet taste with a fragrance is indeed very delicious. However, the lower end of the lotus root must keep the lotus root node, otherwise the sugar juice will seep out. I was very grateful to many friends for taking care of me during this coughing up blood, and I would like to thank them here first.

My Views on the Most Important Work of the Tuberculosis Prevention Association (Continued) 238

— Wang Qizhang

Let's get back to the topic. Now let's talk about the Tuberculosis Prevention Association initiated by Mayor Wu and others. This undertaking is no small matter. In Europe and America, they spend millions upon millions of dollars on such undertakings every year. Now, in our country, which is so financially strapped, how should we start? Here are my personal views. I believe that the first step should be to start with social education and publicity. Why? Because the government is only a guide and planner for health undertakings. When it comes to the quality of actual work, it is definitely beyond the capabilities of a few officials and a small number of technical personnel. It is also necessary to rely on the cooperation of the people. Whether the people can cooperate is definitely not something that can be restrained by laws and punishments. Therefore, the inculcation of basic health knowledge is to enable the people to understand the truth of this kind of work and to happily cooperate. Then, the measures and facilities will easily achieve twice the result with half the effort. For example, cleaning the streets is an important part of municipal work. Now, the sanitation work in Shanghai is not considered unsuccessful. However, people with brains will certainly not desecrate the clean streets. However, trash, urine, feces, paper, vegetable peels, etc. are still thrown and scattered everywhere along the walls and corners. Not desecrating the middle of the road may be due to fear of the law and fear of police intervention and fines. However, in their hearts, they are still a hundred times dissatisfied. I am afraid they will also blame the authorities for being meddlesome. We feel that this kind of incomplete sanitation work and prevention undertaking is just a perfunctory and deceptive ending. We feel that it is too uneconomical. However, the work is already overwhelming. All this is due to the lack of common sense of hygiene among the people. Therefore, I feel that tuberculosis prevention is the most important thing at the moment. It is the educational publicity work of the members.

Although the spread of tuberculosis does not choose classes, the poor, that is, the proletariat, are relatively more difficult to prevent. Because sanitation and disease prevention facilities are often related to economic strength. Therefore, the proper improvement and disposal of clothing, food, housing, and even appropriate treatment is easier for the propertied class. However, for the problem of common sense, the national conditions of our country are different. According to the usual practice of various countries, education must be based on assets. The proletariat is ignorant and weak because they have no education fees. Above the middle class, none are exempt from higher education. Therefore, the propertied class can be said to be the intellectual class. In our China, children's education is not taken seriously. There are families with very rich assets, but their families, even if they are illiterate, are ignorant. Perhaps because of doting, they are not allowed to go to school. Perhaps because of comfort, they are unwilling to study. Sons of Jing Shu are everywhere. In addition, there is also the education they have received, which is still a relic of the closed era, filled with old knowledge restricted by old ideas, and unable to absorb some fresh air. If you say he hasn't received education, he does chew on words and know "Zhi Hu Zhe Ye". Picking up a pen, he can write thousands of words without difficulty. Even those who call themselves doctors, who talk about metaphysics, are like this. In fact, their thinking is outdated and they have no world view or modern common sense. However, they cannot but be listed among the intellectual class and the propertied class. Such people are everywhere. Often Zheng and Shen mix up music and often Zheng and Shen mix up music. This is the most likely to ruin things. Confucius said, "Village elder, the thief of virtue," is a deeply hateful and painful saying. We should also try to save them. Therefore, social education and publicity work, under our current social circumstances, must be divided into two parts. One part is lower-level work, and the other part is upper-level work. As for the method, the authorities, if they use it properly, do not have to adhere to their own opinions. Moreover, sometimes, they may have to adapt to circumstances to make it easier for the people to impress their brains. However, the simplest knowledge of publicity on the brain must at least inculcate the following points, so that the people can recognize the targets:

(1) Tuberculosis is not a hereditary disease, it is an infectious disease. (2)

Tuberculosis can infect many people and can bankrupt a family. (3) The route of transmission is from the sputum that is coughed up, dries up, and scatters into the air with dust, or from the saliva stars (foam) coughed up by seriously ill people, which are inhaled into the lungs. However, the air exhaled by the patient does not contain the virus. (4) Milk is the most appropriate. Drink it boiled. (5) Sputum should be spit into a spittoon. Do not spit indiscriminately.

(6) Develop the habit of breathing through the nose. Especially in dusty and unhygienic areas, never breathe with your mouth open. (7)

At least take a bath once or twice a week to clean your body. It is even better to practice cold water scrubbing to prevent colds. (8) Do not approach people living together who are suspected of having lung disease. (9) Factories, schools, stations, banks, companies, telegraph offices, and public institutions, as well as places where people gather, must be equipped with spittoons. (10) When sweeping the floor, be sure to sprinkle water first. Special attention should be paid to the students on duty in elementary schools.

In our China, because education is not yet universal, school education is only an inculcation for a part of the people. According to the current level of the people in society, those who have received old education and those who have not received education still account for the majority. Only social education can remedy one or two. As for the topic of prevention facilities, it is related to the country's finances. At present, how much power can there be? I dare not speak rashly. I will not discuss it for now.

An Appeal to the Concession Authorities Regarding Unequal Treatment in Public Health 239

— Song Guobin

How can the Chinese Ratepayers' Association remain silent?

Everyone knows that the concessions and the Chinese areas are different. In terms of all public utilities,

the concessions are naturally better than the Chinese areas. The first reason is that the residents

of the concessions pay higher taxes, and the second is that foreigners handle things

better than the Chinese.

However, upon careful observation, the so-called concessions cannot be regarded as a single entity.

There are clearly two different divisions: the Chinese area and the Western area. Therefore, the treatment is also unequal! As long as one

observes slightly from various aspects, one can distinguish who is in the Chinese area and who is in the

Western area.

Now, let's just talk about public health: in the so-called Western area

, the streets are quiet, except for the occasional "heavy traffic," and there is nothing else out of place. The roads are under repair all year round.

The sanitation workers are cleaning all day long, the trees on both sides are neatly arranged

, and one never hears the sound of peddlers selling miscellaneous goods in the alleys, nor does one ever smell any foul odors. If we only look at the situation in this kind of

area, we will undoubtedly praise the concession authorities. However, if we turn around and look at what the so-called Chinese area is like, it is almost

the complete opposite! The streets are extremely noisy and filthy. The roads paved with cobblestones

are extremely inconvenient to walk on, and some places are simply never repaired all year round. Fish stalls, meat counters, all kinds of miscellaneous items are lined up along the roads! The strangest thing is that in front of the entrance of a charity hospital established by a Chinese on a certain road, countless vegetable stalls are lined up. A stinky, fishy smell

makes people want to cover their noses and pass by, which will certainly affect the hospital's hygiene, and

patients also feel a layer of disgust when entering and leaving. The difference between the Chinese area and the Western area is truly like the difference between heaven and hell!

In the same concession, paying the same taxes, the people living in the concession

bear the same financial obligations to the concession authorities, but the treatment by the concession

authorities is not the same at all. It is completely unequal. This one aspect of public health

is enough to represent the rest!

Concession authorities! Human beings have compassion. Unequal

treatment is ultimately not something that civilized people should have! If you have not paid attention to the various things mentioned above in the past, then please pay special attention to them.

Finally! The Chinese Ratepayers' Association cannot shirk its responsibility either. As the representative organization of all

Chinese in the concession, it has always remained silent about the discriminatory treatment suffered by the Chinese. This kind of "fear of foreigners" mentality and "occupying a position without doing any work" spirit cannot but make us suspicious!

A Word to Young Practitioners of Traditional Medicine (Continued) 240

— Jiang Huiming

If you believe my words, then traditional medicine should be abolished. However, it is also necessary to weigh the urgency.

The principles of traditional medicine should indeed be abolished, but traditional Chinese medicine is not without value for reorganization. However, it must be reorganized using scientific medicine. The past is gone, the future can be pursued. I cannot bear to advocate actively abolishing traditional medicine in order to establish a sectarian view. I only hope that my aspiring young people will emulate the Japanese people during the Meiji Restoration, uphold a firm and resolute spirit, (go straight

forward, embrace science, study the truth, do not look ahead, do not look back, do not go back and forth again, do not enter a maze, and perhaps there will be hope.

(4) Recognize the Devilry of the Current So-called Scientificization of Traditional Medicine

When we study a certain subject, we should first have a concept. Scientific matters

proceed step by step, allowing no ambiguity. If one wants to enter the realm of the scientific world, one must

rely on science. Therefore, all non-scientific arguments and non-scientific

behaviors must not be mixed or entangled, confusing black and white. Only then can one speak of scientificization, and only then can one speak of scientific reorganization.

Today, well-known figures in the field of traditional medicine only know that traditional medicine must be reorganized scientifically,

but they lack historical and scientific concepts. They merely pick up a few new terms to

embellish their arguments, even falsely claiming that the truths discovered by science have long been contained in our

ancient Chinese medical books, shamelessly deceiving themselves and others, distorting and forcing connections, without shedding the traditional bad habits of vanity, arrogance, and self-reliance. This does not help the actual practice of medicine in the slightest. On the contrary, it leads to empty talk, creating a devilish path that is neither donkey nor horse. Let me give an example:

Regarding Ying and Wei, some say that Ying and Wei are the functions of dispersing heat and creating heat. Some

say that Ying and Wei are endocrine glands. Regarding the Triple Burner, some say that the Triple Burner is the lymphatic

system. Some say that the Triple Burner is the peritoneum. Regarding the kidneys and the Gate of Life, some say that they

are the adrenal glands. Some say that they are the seminal vesicles. There is endless debate and no consensus.

Such misunderstandings of science and forced associations with mysterious principles, calling it scientificization with a beautiful name, are as far from reality as heaven is from earth? My aspiring young people! What influence and benefit does such absurd theory have on modern medicine? How can it help reorganize traditional medicine?

If we look at it from the perspective of historical research, it also has its historical value. The so-called scientificization of traditional medicine is just a

page in the history of modern medicine, an insignificant work. We must know that scientific medicine is a product of the era after folk medicine. As science gradually rises and metaphysics gradually declines, it is the highway of human

evolution in scholarship. Therefore, what is the need for us to communicate between new and old medicine at present? We can only strive to build new scientific medicine.

(5) Conclusion

Only the brave can accept the truth of facts, and only the wise can find a way out from the facts. Now, please study the above-mentioned issues from an objective standpoint. Its true intention is to

open up a broad and smooth path in medicine from the truth of past events. Where to go and what to do, I await your reflection.

(Comment by Pang Jingzhou) In my article "A Bird's-Eye View," whenever I touch on academic matters, I

loudly call out that if one wants to reorganize old learning, one must first renew old medicine.

Merely creating novelty is not enough to deceive the world. I also once said that the enlightened young practitioners of traditional medicine

bear the heaviest and greatest responsibility. The verification between new and old theories depends entirely on you

as messengers. In the second collection of Mr. Yunxiu's "On Medical Revolution," in the article "A Transformation

to the Group of Old Practitioners of Medicine in Lu," he also praised Jiang Shaoyuan, Tan Cizhong, and Shi Jinmo

for advocating reform, which is a sign that people's hearts are not dead.

He was deeply delighted by this. However, Mr. Yu's article was written in December of the eighteenth year of the Republic of China. Four years have passed since then. I have not heard of any further enlightenment in the field of traditional medicine. Could it be that people's hearts are dead again? Or is it that professional work harms ambition?

In April of this year, Zhou Dadao, Fan Tianpan, and others initiated the National Medicine Review Society. The monthly magazine they published

is generally able to criticize the rights and wrongs of traditional medicine with an objective eye. This is what is meant by a group that is renewing itself. I am also deeply delighted by this. Therefore, I once introduced an article by Zhou Sha jun to this publication. I also praised Zhou, Fan, and the other gentlemen. However, stubborn and foolish people still think that I am using young people

as a tool to attack traditional medicine. This is truly what is meant by idle talk that cannot be understood.

And the National Medicine Review was suddenly forced to cease publication. I was truly disappointed.

He has already heard of the outdated practice of traditional medicine. And now he is a student at the Southeast Medical College. As a practicing traditional doctor, he has re-entered a new medical college. Then, his renewal is even above others. The more he sees the old learning, the more he knows its absurdity. He dares not mislead people with it. Readers, when you read Mr. Jiang's article, you should not think that my previous babbling was superfluous. (The End)

Common Knowledge Q&A About Diseases 241

— Cheng Hanzhang

(19) Asthma

Q: What is asthma?

A: It is a disease caused by the spasmodic contraction of the smallest bronchioles in the lungs. It is related to the nervous system.

Q: What is asthma called in Western languages, and what other names does it have in Chinese?

A: In Western languages, it is Asthma bronchiale, which translates directly to bronchial asthma. In Chinese, it was formerly called Xiao Chuan (哮喘).

Q: What are the causes of this disease?

A: There are many causes: First, heredity, such as those with nervous disorders, arthritis constitution, exudative constitution, etc. Second, skin diseases, such as eczema, measles, etc. Third, nasal cavity diseases, such as nasal polyps, hypertrophic rhinitis, etc. Fourth, bronchial mucosal inflammation and pulmonary tuberculosis. Fifth, endocrine and gonadal disorders, such as goiter, irregular menstruation in women, and pregnant women, etc. Sixth, wandering nerves and the growth of tumors. Seventh, food, animals, plant products (such as animal hair, pollen, etc.), parasitic worms, etc., can all cause the onset of this disease.

Q: What are the special characteristics of the appearance of patients with asthma?

A: Most have weak bones, lack subcutaneous fat, and appear weak at first glance.

Q: What symptoms appear when asthma attacks?

A: The patient suddenly experiences severe difficulty breathing, a strong feeling of pressure in the chest, and a sense of terror. It often occurs at night, suddenly requiring the patient to get out of bed, with cold sweat on the forehead, distended jugular veins, and a purplish-blue color on the lips and tip of the nose. At the end of the attack, there is a slight cough, expectorating a small amount of gray-white viscous sputum.

Q: How is the sputum different from ordinary sputum?

A: The sputum often contains a spiral body called Curschmann's spirals, as well as a crystal body called Charcot-Leyden crystals.

Q: How long does such an attack usually last?

A: It lasts for about thirty to forty minutes; some can even last for days.

Q: Does the patient have a fever?

A: Usually, there is no fever.

Q: What symptoms are there during the intervals between attacks? Can the patient work?

A: There are no symptoms, and they can work as usual.

Q: How should asthma be treated?

A: During an attack, only symptomatic treatment can be performed. This involves having the patient inhale nitrite salts, belladonna leaves, stramonium, etc., and the fumes of saltpeter. Inject atropine sulfate, epinephrine, ephedrine, pituitary extract, etc. Among these, ephedrine is the most effective and can also be taken orally.

Q: How can it be prevented?

A: First, treat nasal diseases, bronchitis, etc. Regulate bowel movements and avoid overeating. Have the patient move to a coastal or mountainous area for convalescence. Medications that can be taken orally include iodine preparations, bromine preparations, arsenic preparations, and thyroid preparations, etc.

The Origin of Pharmacognosy 242

— Zhao Fanhuang

In primitive times, the lives of humans were almost no different from those of apes. Subjected to the threats of wind, rain, thunder, and lightning every day, and attacked by floods and fierce beasts, the suffering from disasters and diseases was severe. Naturally, people used their simple imagination to believe that they were caused by gods and monsters. Thus, shamanic medicine, divination, and fortune-telling arose to treat disasters. The origin of religion is also based on this. Furthermore, primitive people lived among nature, making a living in bushes of grass and trees, and trying the fruits and seeds they found was a natural tendency. Among them, those that were delicious and edible became food. Those that were bitter and unpleasant, when occasionally eaten, either had the effect of treating diseases or caused poisoning. From this experience of hardship, various so-called folk medicines were discovered. Today, when we examine the origins of important drugs, many of them were already used by primitive peoples long ago. For example, cocaine, the darling of local anesthetics today, did it not come from the coca leaves favored by the natives of South America? Opium, a painkiller, was discovered by the ancient Arab people. Tea, a stimulant, was long appreciated by the people of ancient China. Countless other crude drugs have been transformed from folk medicines.

The experimental ancestor of folk medicine, who formed a glorious page in the history of Eastern civilization, was none other than Shennong of our country, who tasted hundreds of herbs. According to the Western calendar, this was probably thousands of years before the Christian era, long before the beginning of Western medicine. However, in ancient times, the study of medicine had no other academic theories or scientific instruments to assist it. People generally knew that something was so, but did not know why. They simply relied on the inherent abilities of human beings, using their sensitive senses to perceive useful materials in their environment and experimenting with them. When pursuing theories, they inevitably resorted to speculations about Yin, Yang, cold, and heat, and discussions about shape, color, odor, and taste, setting up various empty and obscure hypotheses to explain them. These explanations did not necessarily correspond to the facts, and therefore it was difficult to form a systematic theory. This is what distinguishes it from the scientific medicine of later generations, which must be established only after names and realities are matched. However, the experiences gained by the ancients based on facts are by no means without value. We can indeed extract the truth from their rich experiences, discarding the falsehoods. Using natural science as a basis, we can study them and understand them through experiments to form a rational explanation. This is why ancient herbal records, both Chinese and foreign, have the same need for reference and discussion in today's medical development, in the textual research of herbal studies, and in the research of pharmacognosy, and why they are valued by countries all over the world and have not been abolished to this day. There is a good reason for this.

Pharmacognosy and Western Herbal Studies 243

What is now called pharmacognosy is what was called herbal studies in ancient times. Therefore, to understand today's pharmacognosy, one should first know ancient herbal studies. According to Western sources, the earliest herbal studies were inspired by rudimentary botany. Because botany was a pure science at the time, it only sought to clarify the truth, regardless of other purposes. Western medicine would not have come about without the spirit of ancient Greek science, and the philosophers of the Roman era would not have known to study the use of materials to improve people's lives. During the first century AD, among those with abundant knowledge of plant taxonomy, Dioscorides (DioscorideCa6A·D·) focused on the uses of plants, created an artificial classification of plants, and described 600 kinds of medicinal plants. His theories did not stick to pure botany, but rather guided the formation of an applied botanical herbal study. Dioscorides' academic contribution to botany was truly not inferior to that of Theophrastus (370-285B·C·) (a botanist before Linnaeus in the Greek era). At that time, he had already divided plants into spices, foods, and medicinal materials, and demonstrated the scope of plant utilization. From a scientific point of view, he broke away from philosophy and pure botany to create an applied scientific herbal study. The benefits that humanity has gained are not small. Dioscorides' herbal studies enjoyed great reputation at the time. Until the Renaissance, between the fourteenth and fifteenth centuries, it had a dominant influence.

The so-called herbalists not only collected plants, animals, and minerals but also used them for treatment in natural science (Historianaturalis). This is the same approach that has been used in both the East and the West. Therefore, herbal studies, regardless of China or other countries, have survived until today. Furthermore, the only difference between East and West herbal studies in the past is that Western herbalists mostly came after the so-called Rhizotomi (root gatherers). Hippocrates (Hippocrates460-377B·C·), the great physician, was a student of Aristotle (Aristotte384-322 B.C.), the great philosopher. The great botanist Theophrastus (who wrote "Historia Pantarum," recording over 500 species of plants) was made possible. These scholars laid the foundation for science, and the herbal era turned into the botanical era and progressed far. Therefore, the path of medicine eventually converged. In the East, Shennong was born and passed down the "Shennong's Herbal Classic." Although wise rulers and famous philosophers of past generations have all relied on this book, making changes, deletions, and revisions, they have only been limited to the field of herbal studies and have never reached the realm of pure science. Now, if we compare the herbal studies of the East and West, we know that the herbal studies and the progress of botany in the West have been progressing side by side. Chinese herbal studies have developed independently. Because they were not supplemented by botany and other sciences from the beginning, they have ultimately become stuck in a rut. It is truly regrettable. (To be continued)

Using Chinese Medicine in the West (Continued) 244

— Zhou Mengbai

(16) Coptis

The original product belongs to the Ranunculaceae family. It is collected by digging up the rhizomes that have been growing for seven or eight years, removing the fibrous roots, and drying them in the sun for use. There are many varieties: including Coptis Anemonaefolia S·etz·, Coptis Branchypetala S·etz·, Coptis Branchypetala S·etz·Var Pygmaca·Miq·, Coptis Orientalis, Maxim·, etc.

Characteristics: This product is usually curved, with numerous small branch roots. The top has remnants of petioles. The outside is dark yellow, with nodular growths everywhere. The broken surface is sharp and rough, odorless, and extremely bitter. Chewing it stains the saliva yellow.

Ingredients: The most important ingredient in this product is berberine (BerberinC20H19Na5). However, according to recent research, in addition to berberine, there are also palmatine (PalmatinC20H21N05) and columbamine (ColumbaminC21H19N05) extracts. However, since these two ingredients are also contained in Colombo Root (Radix Colnmbo), it is known that Coptis and Colombo Root are similar.

Uses: This product is a bitter stomachic. Because its ingredients are similar to those of Colombo, it can also be used as a substitute for Colombo Root.

(Appendix on Old Theories) It is very bitter and very cold, enters the heart, drains fire, calms the liver, cools the blood, 丨丨All treatments for blood: Ledebouriella seseloides is used for the upper part, Coptis is used for the middle part, and Sanguisorba officinalis is used for the lower part. 丨丨Dries dampness, opens depression, eliminates irritability, quenches thirst, benefits the liver and gallbladder, thickens the intestines and stomach, eliminates heart stasis, treats intestinal disorders, dysentery, fullness, chest pain, hidden beams, alcohol poisoning, improves vision, calms fright, eliminates malnutrition, and kills roundworms.

According to Li Shizhen, there are two types of Coptis: one with thick roots, no hairs, and nodules, like eagle chicken claws, and solid, with a deep yellow color; the other with no nodules, many hairs, empty in the middle, and a faded yellow color. Each has its own suitable uses. However, what is used today is generally regardless of shape, fat or thin, choosing the deep yellow and solid ones. The quality is light and empty, or with a black color, which is an inferior product and cannot be used.

(Note) Although Coptis is a Chinese medicine, almost all of what is used by Chinese medicine practitioners today is Japanese Coptis. It is not only cheaper, but also has a firm texture and a yellow color. Although the Chinese Pharmacopoeia lists Chinese Coptis (Coptis Chinensis Franch), its characteristics and organization are all based on the Japanese Tanba Coptis. Whether they are the same should be proven by testing when the Chinese Pharmacopoeia is revised. This article is also mostly based on Tanba Coptis, and I am very sorry for not correcting the errors!

Overview of Meningitis (II) 245

— Wang Xiaolan

The symptoms of meningitis in those afflicted with the disease are of two types: typical and atypical. Typical symptoms, after the pathogen is transmitted, have an incubation period of several hours, or one or two days, or three or four days, followed by a sudden onset of chills and shivering, accompanied by a high fever reaching 39 degrees Celsius or higher. The head feels severely painful, especially in the back. Vertigo, vomiting, agitation, and restlessness, convulsions in the limbs, and stiffness of the neck occur. If the disease affects the spinal meninges, the spine, waist, and back may also be in severe pain. Patients cannot bear the suffering, often crying aloud. The whole body's senses are keenly sensitive, fearing being touched by others. Strong light and loud noises are both to be avoided. Herpes labialis often appears on the lips and face, and roseola or erythema may occasionally appear on the trunk and limbs.

As spasms increase, it leads to trismus (lockjaw), opisthotonos (arching of the back), and sinking of the abdomen like the bottom of a boat. If the patient's knees are bent close to the abdomen, joint flexion and extension become impaired; in medicine, this is called Kernig's sign. Furthermore, the vasomotor nerves of the skin are abnormally excited, and slight friction with hard objects will leave red marks for a long time; in medicine, this is called Trousseau's sign. When the disease reaches the base of the brain and invades the optic nerve, the pupils differ in size and light reflex diminishes. When it invades the auditory nerve, it causes tinnitus and difficulty hearing. If the oculomotor and facial nerves are paralyzed, it manifests as a distorted face and strabismus (squint). If the disease reaches the cerebral cortex, it can further cause hemiplegia, paraplegia, speech disorders, and local spasms.

The fever pattern of this disease is indefinite, breathing is irregular, and joint swelling and pain and spleen enlargement often occur. Consciousness is muddled and unclear, with delirium, lethargy, and even a comatose state all day long. Infants may also have a bulging fontanelle and regurgitation. At the onset of the disease, the pulse is slow, bowel movements and urination are not smooth, and tendon and skin reflexes are all keenly sensitive. In the later stage, because the vagus nerve's initial excitation wanes, the pulse becomes frequent, and spasms turn into paralysis, so bowel and bladder control is often lost, and reflexes are either diminished or absent. In severe cases approaching death, body temperature is often elevated. Death is often caused by cerebral paralysis or heart failure.

Atypical symptoms: may only feel headache, fever, vomiting, and stiff neck, healing within a few days, called abortive meningitis; or operating as usual, suddenly developing chills, high fever, spasms, and fainting, quickly leading to death, called fulminant meningitis. There is also sudden loss of consciousness, hemiplegia, similar to stroke, called apoplectic meningitis; and even symptoms that are sometimes mild, sometimes severe, recurring, lasting for weeks or months, called intermittent meningitis. In addition, there are cases of endocarditis and other complications during the illness, which have been described in the pathology section, so they will not be repeated here.

The course and prognosis of meningitis: The course and prognosis of this disease vary with the symptoms. The typical course usually lasts about two or three weeks. Those who recover after treatment gradually improve after one or two weeks and heal day by day. However, sequelae such as headache, dizziness, strabismus, blindness, deafness, idiocy, aphasia, walking difficulties, cerebral edema, muscle stiffness, or paralysis of one or two parts of the body often remain. In severe cases, life is lost within the second week due to increased cerebral symptoms or cardiac paralysis. Among the atypical cases, only the abortive type can recover within a few days. The fulminant type progresses rapidly and is difficult to treat. The intermittent type often leads to death due to prolonged illness and debilitation or complications.

The mortality rate of this disease, according to historical statistics, varies depending on the degree of epidemic, the severity of symptoms, and the appropriateness of treatment. In many cases, it reaches 80%, and in few cases, it is 20%, averaging more than half. Infants are especially numerous. Even if those who contract the disease are cured, sequelae often remain. Brainpower is impaired in children, intelligence is low, and academics are inevitably affected. Those who can fully recover their health are rare.

Diagnosis of Meningitis: When this disease is prevalent, it is not difficult to diagnose if symptoms such as those described above are found. However, to obtain definitive evidence, secretions from the nasopharynx or cerebrospinal fluid must be collected and cultured for pathogens; and stained and examined under a microscope to find the inherent intracellular meningococcal diplococcus. However, there are many similar symptoms to this disease, so the differences are listed below for differentiation:

(1) Tuberculous Meningitis: This disease generally has a long-term prodromal stage, such as headache, fever, nausea, and vomiting, which slowly develop. There is often a hereditary constitution for tuberculosis, and tuberculous manifestations in the skin, bones, lymph nodes, lungs, fundus, etc., can be demonstrated. There is no herpes labialis. Furthermore, the spinal fluid is transparent and contains tubercle bacilli.

(2) Purulent Meningitis: The patient's body must first have a pus-filled cavity such as parotitis, purulent otitis media, erysipelas, or osteomyelitis. Herpes labialis and arthritis are rarely found during the illness. If the pathogens in the cerebrospinal fluid are examined, they are also different.

(3) Typhoid Fever: This disease has a unique fever pattern, a slow course, and often causes abdominal symptoms such as tympanites (bloating). There is no herpes labialis. If the Widal agglutination test is performed, or the cerebrospinal fluid is examined for pathogens, it can be clarified.

(4) Septicopyemia: Examination of the blood can reveal pathogens. Examination of the cerebrospinal fluid is especially easy to distinguish.

(5) Cerebral Hemorrhage: This disease is similar to apoplectic meningitis, but there are no symptoms such as stiff neck, spinal pain, fever, keen sensitivity of the senses, or herpes labialis.

(6) Influenza: This disease often causes severe upper respiratory tract inflammation. If suspected, the pathogens in the nasopharyngeal secretions can be examined to clarify.

(7) Pneumonia: This disease has rapid breathing and specific lung symptoms, and rusty sputum is coughed up, so it is easy to distinguish.

(8) Acute Miliary Tuberculosis: This disease has rapid pulse and breathing, and tubercle bacilli are mixed in the spinal fluid. Examination of the choroid can further reveal tuberculous nodules.

Treatment of Meningitis: (1) Nursing Method: Those suffering from this disease must have peace of mind. Ice pillows or cold, wet cloths should be applied to the head to relieve pain, as well as to the spine. The oral cavity and pharynx should be gargled with disinfectant solutions, such as hydrogen peroxide and potassium chlorate solution. If bowel movements are obstructed, an enema should be given. If urinary retention occurs, a rubber catheter should be used for urination. The light in the sickroom should be dim, and the air should be clean. All stimuli such as loud noises and bright lights should be avoided. For diet, easily digestible liquids rich in nutrients, such as milk, arrowroot flour, and thin porridge, are best. If the illness gradually recovers, a warm bath may be given appropriately. For those with weakened muscles, electrical therapy and massage can be used.

(2) Serum Therapy: Meningitis serum contains antibodies that can kill bacteria and remove toxins, with great efficacy. In the past, the mortality rate was 70-80%, but recently, with the application of serum, it can be reduced to 20-30%. However, the disease comes on very suddenly, so the earlier it is used, the better. The injection site should be in the spinal groove, as this can directly reach the subarachnoid space, making it more effective than subcutaneous or intramuscular injections. The amount should be determined by the condition and the amount of cerebrospinal fluid extracted, usually about 20-40 cc. For young and weak individuals, it can be appropriately reduced according to age and constitution. If the symptoms do not subside and the body temperature remains high, it can be continued every other day. If toxins have entered the blood, intravenous injection should be performed concurrently. When arthritis occurs, it can also be injected into the joint cavity. (To be continued)

Free Talk

I Also Talk About Jin Shengtan 246

— Chen Zizhan

The inaugural issue of "Literature" contains an article by Mr. Lu Xun discussing Jin Shengtan. If Jin Shengtan had a spirit underground, he would surely approve. However, Mr. Lu Xun only saw the bad side of Jin Shengtan, while his good side also had undeniable merits. Take his views on novels, for example. He lived in an era when the eight-legged essay and traditional classical literature were thriving. He elevated the status of vernacular novels in literature, not considering it "a minor branch of literature." He taught his ten-year-old son to read Water Margin, and he advised beginners to read Water Margin, believing that the writing of Water Margin was rigorous and that reading Water Margin would lead to understanding the method of reading all books. He believed that the spirit and principles of Water Margin were as clear, bright, light, and refreshing as one or two sections of the Analects. He also believed that the writing of Water Margin had the same rigor as Zhuangzi and Records of the Grand Historian. However, he did not teach beginners to read ancient books like the Analects and Zhuangzi. What kind of insight is this? Is it merely "picking up the leftovers of Yuan Hongdao"? Wouldn't it shame today's old conservatives?

As for his criticism of Water Margin and Romance of the West Chamber, and even Zhuangzi, Sorrow of Parting, Records of the Grand Historian, and Du Fu's poetry, "all of them are forcibly dragged into the methods of eight-legged essays," as Mr. Lu Xun said. However, we must know that using the methods of eight-legged essays to measure other literature has been a common habit of general literati since the mid-Ming Dynasty. This fault cannot be entirely attributed to Jin Shengtan. It goes without saying that Li Zhuowu and Zhong Bokijing's commentaries on novels were the same. Even Gui Youguang, a master of classical prose, commented on Records of the Grand Historian, and Tang Jingchuan and Mao Lumen commented on the prose of the Eight Great Masters of the Tang and Song Dynasties, weren't they also using the methods of eight-legged essays?

One more point, Jin Shengtan, because of his hatred for the roving bandits, in addition to often attaching some Spring and Autumn Annals' legal principles in his commentaries, "cut off the latter half of Water Margin, dreaming of a Ji Shuye to kill all the Song Jiangs, which is also foolish enough." Mr. Lu Xun's comments are very accurate, and I have no humble opinions to add. At most, I can only say that Jin Shengtan was killed for participating in the legal movement to resist corrupt officials (i.e., the crying at the temple case), which just proves that even resisting bad governments in a certain way is not necessarily reprehensible.

In short, Jin Shengtan elevated the literary value of novels and dramas, and resisted literary traditionalism. He and Li Yu can be considered the two great eccentrics in the literary world during the Ming and Qing dynasties. Moreover, Jin Shengtan ultimately died for resisting corrupt officials, which seems worthy of sympathy from those with aspirations.

Shi Zhenlin's "Small Notes" 247

— Yin Chuan

Mentioning Shi Zhenlin (Wugang), probably everyone will think of his "Miscellaneous Records of Xiqing"; but what I want to talk about is the rarely seen "Hua Yang Scattered Manuscripts" published after "Miscellaneous Records." "Miscellaneous Records" are essays, while "Scattered Manuscripts" are literary collections. The content of "Scattered Manuscripts" mainly records people, events, travel, and academic discussions; it includes many of his own poems. He also had unique insights on poetry, as he said in the "Preface to Shu Qiutang's Poems": "To take Tang poetry as a gourd and imitate it is dull; to take Song poetry as Chinese dates and swallow them whole is stupid. Learning Tang poetry is like painting a tiger; the meaning of the tiger is little, and the meaning of the dog is much. Learning Song poetry is like carving a swan; the shape of the swan is fake, and the shape of the duck is real," which is very insightful. Of course, many unusual people are recorded in his writings, such as "Old Man of Lamentation"; the travel essays are also full of novelty. The entire book is in two volumes, and each volume ends with "Small Notes," seventeen entries in the first volume and seven in the second. The excellent ones are no less than the "Miscellaneous Records." For example, the seventh "Small Note" in the second volume says:

In the first day of the second month of the Qianlong Yiyou year, the scenery was clear and beautiful. The poetry disciples of Ju Tai arranged to travel to Ping Mountain. Passing by the Xi Yin Chan Temple, we visited Cheng Chengtan, but he was not there. Passing by the Fan Li Guan Zhou Binru Ancient Taoist Temple, we met Ni Sheng Ziwen, who offered vegetarian meals. There were many calligraphy and paintings on the walls, and we lamented not coming with Layman Lullu. We inquired about the jade hook grottoes and the news of the jade flowers. We pulled Ni Sheng across the Rainbow Bridge. Fragrance wafted towards us from afar, and the plum blossoms were less than halfway in bloom, welcoming us with smiles, as if wanting to ask for poems, and we lamented not arranging to come with Jiang Lang. We passed by the Fa Hai Temple without entering, called for a ferry to the west, and watched the wild cranes on Plum Island, walking leisurely and calmly, appearing and disappearing behind the flowers. We recited aloud with Ju Tai the astonishing lines of Jiang Lang and lamented not being able to compose poems together, so we returned without reaching Ping Mountain. We said goodbye to Ni Sheng, took a detour to wait for Layman Lullu in the evening, and ordered wine. We said goodbye and returned, recording it with five ancient poems, asking old friends Zhenting and Mokeng, Qinzhuang, Zhiyuan, Zhenxi, Yutian, and Liangzhai to compose responses, and also sending them to Xiqin for harmony. The flowers on Jiang Lang's pen will compete to bloom before the red plum blossoms!

However, although there are many masterpieces in the "Small Notes," especially the meditative "Small Notes," I especially dislike reading them, except for a few exceptions. The main reason for this is that the "Small Notes," it can be said, the entire "Hua Yang Scattered Manuscripts," mostly reflect the author's thoughts after converting to Buddhism in his later years, so they are all about cause and effect. Those that do not involve this point are very few. Perhaps the reason why "Scattered Manuscripts" cannot circulate like "Miscellaneous Records" lies in this. The entire book is written in a strong and vigorous style, and the use of words is quite original, such as in the article "Recording Ma Shouchou," where Zhenlin describes his travels, uses verbs vividly, and truly gives people a sense of endless changes.

Sitting by the Sea 248

— Lin Huiyin

I don't know why, but in my heart, I secretly hoped that some acquaintance would come, even if it was someone I often met and only greeted briefly without really talking, even just an ordinary acquaintance with polite conversation. But the tea was fading layer by layer, and yet no acquaintance came. Although I didn't know why I had such a hope, it seemed because I had a hope that I didn't want to leave, and I didn't think of any other place to go.

Not only was the tea fading layer by layer, but my appetite was also full, unable to be fuller. But still, no acquaintance came. Now, although I hadn't thought of any other place to go, it seemed the time had come when I couldn't help but leave.

But because I had to go, several places came to my mind, touting their merits, and I chose the seaside among them.

Leaving the station, I walked along the river towards the sea, walking straight until the river met the sea. In the river, sailboats were anchored at almost equal intervals, each with a kerosene lamp. The moon was just a sliver, curved, curved so evenly, so enticingly, as if challenging someone's eyebrows.

The light on the lighthouse was blinking on and off, and not far from it stood an inn, seemingly hypnotized by the blinking light of the lighthouse, falling into a sleeping state.

Pacing back and forth a couple of times, I wanted to sit, so I walked into the inn. The inn gradually woke up, and finally, light also shone in the dining room.

I just wanted to sit, so I only ordered a cup of coffee.

Not long after I sat down, a dog came over. As if familiar with me, it crouched down by my feet, looking at me intimately. After looking for a while, it stood up and walked away; after walking for a while, it crouched down by my feet again. Soon, it fell asleep, as if it had received some comfort.

In that room that wasn't exactly small, there were only two beings, the dog and me. The dog was asleep, and seemed to be sleeping very sweetly. As for the one who was awake, I don't know why, but my heart was beating very fast. In such a quiet setting, for my heart to beat so fast seemed to have no reason. But my heart was racing for no reason.

Maybe it was because it was too quiet that my heart was beating so fast? So I thought of waking the dog up. But I didn't really wake it up. I just looked at it, intimately, as if it were a close companion of mine. I didn't want to wake it up. I wanted it to sleep, to sleep even sweeter. So I sat there, in that quiet room, and no longer attempted to find the reason why my heart was beating so fast.

On "Understanding Reality" 249

— Xu Maoyong

After two months, Mr. Shiheng suddenly remembered that someone had once "pointed out" his opinion and made the wrong criticism, so he remotely chased after it to "oppose." This was quite surprising to me, who wrote that article, and at the same time, I felt very embarrassed. Should I say a few more words? I was afraid that Mr. Shiheng and a third party would suspect me of being argumentative or competitive. If I remained silent, I would feel quite wronged. Since the publication of "Miscellaneous Talk About Little Ghosts" in Free Talk, the unexpected troubles it has stirred up have been too numerous!

Speaking of it, it was a small缘分 (yuanfen, predestined affinity). I have never paid attention to the literary criticism of Chinese critics. But the reason why I paid attention to Mr. Shiheng's article criticizing Sha Ning and read out some feelings was because of what Mr. Ba Jin said. Mr. Ba Jin once said to me: "In terms of literary criticism, Han Shiheng is very promising. He has not published many critical texts, but his research on literature is indeed very deep." It was the influence of these words that made me pay attention to Mr. Shiheng's article and trust him very much.

When he criticized Sha Ning, thinking that Sha Ning this person "is not a historical archetype" but "completely the fruit of the artist's fantasy, that is, the author's ideal character," I completely agreed. But when he said that Sha Ning's author was weak in artistic production, "resulting in something very exaggerated and very artificial," I offered a bit of supplementary opinion.

My opinion is very simple, namely: (1) Exaggeration and artificiality are unavoidable for any writer, no matter how good. Even the "historical archetypes" in Turgenev's writing have a lot of exaggeration and artificiality. (2) The reason why Sha Ning does not become a typical figure of an era is fundamentally because there is no such figure in society (in other words, this is entirely the fruit of the artist's fantasy), which has little to do with the author's artistic production. At the time, I originally wanted to say something about Artzybasheff's artistic power, thinking that to say his artistic production was weak was setting too high a standard, especially for today's Chinese writers. Those who are slightly inferior to Turgenev are considered weak. Mr. Shiheng's criticism is really harsh!

However, at that time, I was not specifically discussing with Mr. Shiheng, so this idea was not written out. The reason why I am writing it here now is to let Mr. Shiheng know that I cannot agree with lightly asserting that Artzybasheff is superficial. (To be continued)

Two Brothers (41) 250

— Guy de Maupassant, Translated by Li Weike

Had she cheated on his father, she? … His father! Yes, he was an honest, sincere man who did not cut corners in his business, but his thoughts never went beyond the scope of his little shop. This previously very beautiful woman - this he knew, and others could still see now - a woman endowed with an elegant, courteous, and sensitive soul, how could she be willing to become engaged and married to a man so different from herself?

Why pursue it? She had married just like those little girls who, by the order of their parents, were married to boys enjoying dowries. After they married, they immediately lived in the shop on Montmartre Street. The bride, who was in charge of accounting, was inspired by the spirit of that new family, that subtle and sacred concept of common interest that prevailed among most merchant couples in Paris, replacing love or even affection. She began to work with all her lively and meticulous intelligence for the future of their family. And her life had passed in such a monotonous, stable, honest, and unfeeling way! …

Unfeeling?… Could a woman never fall in love? A young and beautiful woman, living in Paris, reading books, praising the heroines who sacrificed themselves for passion on the stage, could she, from youth to old age, keep her heart from being stirred even once? If it was said about another woman, he would not believe it - why did he believe it because it was his mother?

Yes, she was able to fall in love like other women! Because, even though she was his mother, why would she be different from other women?

She had been young, and at that time, she had also had all the poetic faults that troubled the hearts of young men and women. Confined and imprisoned in the shop, living with a vulgar husband who always talked about business, she had dreamed of moonlight, travel, kisses in the darkness, etc. Then, one day, a man appeared in her eyes just like the lovers described in books, and he even spoke to her like the lovers in the books.

She had fallen in love with him. Why not? It was his mother! Come on! Just because she was his mother, did he have to become blind and deny the obvious?

Had she surrendered herself to him?… Of course, because this man had never had other girlfriends; of course, because he always loved the woman who was far away from him and aging, 自然啦(zìrán la - of course), because he left all his property to her son, their son!… So Pierre stood up, trembling with anger, wishing he could kill someone! He stretched out his arms, spread his palms, wanting to strike, smash, crush, strangle! Who? Everyone, his father, his brother, the dead Malaiseau, his mother!

He hurried home. What was he going to do?

As he passed a small tower next to the signal post, the sharp sound of the foghorn suddenly came from in front of him. He was so startled that he almost fell, retreating all the way to the granite railing. He sat on it, no longer having the strength to walk, completely frightened by the sound.

The first ship to respond to the sound, seeming to be very close, was apparently entering the port, as the tide had already risen. Pierre turned around and saw the red eyes of the ship shrouded in fog. Subsequently, a large black shadow emerged between the two embankments under the diffuse glow of the lights on the dock. Behind him, the night watchman, the retired old captain, called out in a hoarse voice:

"What's the ship's name?"

In the fog, the pilot standing on the deck also replied in a hoarse voice:

"Saint-Lucie."

Organization 251

— Wei Ba

Who says the Chinese have no organization? We Chinese have plenty of organizations, many organizations. Let's not talk about the major affairs of the party and the nation. Just talking about ordinary common people, if they want to have some fun, they must start an organization.

We are now a democratic country, so all actions must be carried out in accordance with democratic methods. In a democratic country, it is said that human rights are most important, so holding meetings and collective discussions have become necessary procedures for doing things. To hold a meeting, there must first be a society; to have collective discussions, one must first find people. This is an immutable principle. Thus, there are organizations of various associations.

According to "A Primer on Civil Rights," as long as people gather, they can form a society. Therefore, the number of signs for various "societies" and "associations" in alleys and corners exceeds the number of advertisements for "specializing in treating gonorrhea and leukorrhea." Declarations are issued, grandly; badges are worn, spiritedly. Thus, all 400 million people have organizations, and everyone is a member. Isn't this magnificent!

Dividing them into categories, there are "student associations" during school days; "native place associations" when one goes out; "symposiums" for self-praise and mutual flattery; and "Golden Light Sutra Dharma Assemblies" for praying for peace. In addition, if you want to save the country, you can join the "National Salvation Association"; if you want to fly an airplane, you can join the "Aeronautical Association." Extending this further, there are associations for studying dancing, associations for practicing thrift, associations for handling funerals, and associations for welcoming and sending off important people. As long as you are willing to pay attention, put in the effort, from national planning to small matters of diet, nothing cannot be formed into an association. Although the scale may vary, the organization is essentially the same. "Large" can mean a three-story Western-style building; "small" can mean a space next to the stove. Both can serve as a meeting place and a place for socializing. Seven or eight committee members, ten or twenty members, all acting in a grand manner, how much is truly sincere! People say that the Chinese are like a plate of loose sand; I say that the Chinese are like a piece of sesame candy, because they mingle everywhere and can't be excluded anywhere.

Speaking of the content of the associations, although the signs are different, the purpose is only one: first, to flatter others; second, to flatter oneself. The way to flatter others is either to obtain subsidies for reimbursement or to want to obtain subsidies in order to be of service oneself. Relying on the opinions of others, treating them as one's own, following the banner and shouting, running errands, this is one type. The way to flatter oneself is to boast, make suggestions, issue telegrams, be listed as a committee member, or act as a representative, speak慷慨, follow the prevailing trend, and express indignation at the loss of territory, expressing a wish to be a "backbone" in resistance. In short, one must be sophisticated and appear to be important. If one's name often appears in newspaper news columns, then one will become famous without even trying. If one flatters effectively, one will naturally be flattered into the ranks of "important people"; otherwise, at least one will be a "celebrity." Because today's people are to associations as fish are to water, without them there is no "activity." Here is another formula, followed by the public, which is the saying, "Rather be a driver than a sedan chair carrier." Because although "public opinion" sounds good, "despotism" is ultimately useful. In an association, although there are seven or eight committee members, only one or two people actually do things. Latecomers find it even harder to stand out, only playing supporting roles. Therefore, it is better to form one's own association than to join someone else's. Is this why there are so many associations today?

"Source of Trouble" 252

— Shi Ben

The phrase "concubine offering 'Lanshui'" (a poisonous plant that can cause madness) a few years ago, when my social experience was still immature, I was somewhat skeptical and felt sorry for the concubines, thinking that this was an insulting way to refer to "concubines." Who knew that the unfortunate incident that happened to my relative due to a concubine proved to me and made me suddenly realize and deeply believe that this saying is not wrong.

Originally, my relative Mr. Li, was a wealthy household in the town, with more than 8,000 mu of good farmland in real estate. In the poor and remote X town, he could be considered a top landlord. His family's annual income was entirely based on land rent.

A harmonious and happy family instantly turned into a tragic battlefield of self-slaughter!
